` What be the matter with me ? '
she think , but somehow or other she manage to reach the hut , and throw herself down in a corner , where she sleep so soundly that for day no one be able to wake her .
At length , one morning early , a cock begin to crow so loud that she could sleep no longer and a he continue to crow she seem to understand what he be say , and that he be tell her that Djulung be dead , kill and eat by her sister , and that his bone lay bury under the kitchen fire .
Very softly she get up , and take up the large stone under the fire , and creep out carry the bone to the cave by the fountain , where she dig a hole and bury them anew .
And a she scoop out the hole with a stick she sing a song , bid the bone grow till they become a tree -- a tree that reach up so high into the heaven that it leaf would fall across the sea into another island , whose king would pick them up .
As there be no Djulung to give her rice to , the girl soon become fat again , and a she be able to do her work a of old , her sister do not trouble about her .
They never guess that when she go into the forest to gather her stick , she never fail to pay a visit to the tree , which grow taller and more wonderful day by day .
Never be such a tree see before .
Its trunk be of iron , it leaf be of silk , it flower of gold , and it fruit of diamond , and one evening , though the girl do not know it , a soft breeze take one of the leaf , and blow it across the sea to the foot of one of the king 's attendant .
` What a curious leaf !
I have never behold one like it before .
I must show it to the king , ' he say , and when the king saw it he declare he would never rest until he have find the tree which bore it , even if he have to spend the rest of his life in visit the island that lay all round .
Happily for him , he begin with the island that be nearest , and here in the forest he suddenly saw stand before him the iron tree , it bough cover with shin leaf like the one he carry about him .
` But what sort of a tree be it , and how do it get here ? '
he ask of the attendant he have with him .
No one could answer him , but a they be about to pass out of the forest a little boy go by , and the king stop and inquired if there be anyone living in the neighbourhood whom he might question .
` Seven girl live in a hut down there , ' reply the boy , point with his finger to where the sun be set .
` Then go and bring them here , and I will wait , ' say the king , and the boy run off and tell the sister that a great chief , with string of jewel round his neck , have send for them .
Pleased and excite the six elder sister at once follow the boy , but the young , who be busy , and who do not care about stranger , stay behind , to finish the work she be do .
The king welcome the girl eagerly , and ask them all manner of question about the tree , but a they have never even heard of it existence , they could tell him nothing .
` And if we , who live close by the forest , do not know , you may be sure no one do , ' add the eldest , who be rather cross at find this be all that the king want of them .
` But the boy tell me there be seven of you , and there be only six here , ' say the king .
` Oh , the young be at home , but she be always half asleep , and be of no use except to cut wood for the fire , ' reply they in a breath .
` That may be , but perhaps she dream , ' answer the king .
` Anyway , I will speak to her also . '
Then he sign to one of his attendant , who follow the path that the boy have take to the hut .
Soon the man return , with the girl walk behind him .
And as soon a she reach the tree it bow itself to the earth before her , and she stretch out her hand and pick some of it leaf and flower and give them to the king .
` The maiden who can work such wonder be fit to be the wife of the great chief , ' he say , and so he marry her , and take her with him across the sea to his own home , where they live happily for ever after .
From ` Folk Lore , ' by A. F. Mackenzie .
The Sea King 's Gift There be once a fisherman who be call Salmon , and his Christian name be Matte .
He live by the shore of the big sea ; where else could he live ?
He have a wife call Maie ; could you find a good name for her ?
In winter they dwell in a little cottage by the shore , but in spring they flit to a red rock out in the sea and stay there the whole summer until it be autumn .
The cottage on the rock be even small than the other ; it have a wooden bolt instead of an iron lock to the door , a stone hearth , a flagstaff , and a weather-cock on the roof .
The rock be call Ahtola , and be not large than the market-place of a town .
Between the crevice there grow a little rowan tree and four alder bush .
Heaven only know how they ever come there ; perhaps they be bring by the winter storm .
Besides that , there flourish some tuft of velvety grass , some scattered reed , two plant of the yellow herb call tansy , four of a red flower , and a pretty white one ; but the treasure of the rock consist of three root of garlic , which Maie have put in a cleft .
Rock wall shelter them on the north side , and the sun shone on them on the south .
This do not seem much , but it suffice Maie for a herb plot .
All good thing go in three , so Matte and his wife fish for salmon in spring , for herring in summer , and for cod in winter .
When on Saturdays the weather be fine and the wind favourable , they sail to the near town , sell their fish , and go to church on Sunday .
But it often happen that for week at a time they be quite alone on the rock Ahtola , and have nothing to look at except their little yellow-brown dog , which bore the grand name of Prince , their grass tuft , their bush and bloom , the sea bay and fish , a stormy sky and the blue , white-crested wave .
For the rock lay far away from the land , and there be no green islet or human habitation for mile round , only here and there appear a rock of the same red stone a Ahtola , besprinkle day and night with the ocean spray .
Matte and Maie be industrious , hard-working folk , happy and content in their poor hut , and they think themselves rich when they be able to salt a many cask of fish a they require for winter and yet have some leave over with which to buy tobacco for the old man , and a pound or two of coffee for his wife , with plenty of burn corn and chicory in it to give it a flavour .
Besides that , they have bread , butter , fish , a beer cask , and a buttermilk jar ; what more do they require ?
All would have go well have not Maie be possess with a secret longing which never let her rest ; and this be , how she could manage to become the owner of a cow .
` What would you do with a cow ? '
ask Matte .
` She could not swim so far , and our boat be not large enough to bring her over here ; and even if we have her , we have nothing to fee her on . '
` We have four alder bush and sixteen tuft of grass , ' rejoin Maie .
` Yes , of course , ' laugh Matte , ` and we have also three plant of garlic .
Garlic would be fine feeding for her . '
` Every cow like salt herring , ' rejoin his wife .
` Even Prince be fond of fish . '
` That may be , ' say her husband .
` Methinks she would soon be a dear cow if we have to fee her on salt herring .
All very well for Prince , who fight with the gull over the last morsel .
Put the cow out of your head , mother , we be very well off a we be . '
Maie sigh .
She know well that her husband be right , but she could not give up the idea of a cow .
The buttermilk no longer taste as good a usual in the coffee ; she think of sweet cream and fresh butter , and of how there be nothing in the world to be compare with them .
One day a Matte and his wife be clean herring on the shore they hear Prince barking , and soon there appear a gaily paint boat with three young men in it , steer towards the rock .
They be student , on a boating excursion , and want to get something to eat .
` Bring u a junket , good mother , ' cry they to Maie .
` Ah !
if only I have such a thing ! '
sigh Maie . '
A can of fresh milk , then , ' say the student ; ` but it must not be skim . '
` Yes , if only I have it ! '
sigh the old woman , still more deeply .
` What !
have n't you get a cow ? '
Maie be silent .
This question so strike her to the heart that she could not reply .
` We have no cow , ' Matte answer ; ` but we have good smoke herring , and can cook them in a couple of hour . '
` All right , then , that will do , ' say the student , a they fling themselves down on the rock , while fifty silvery-white herring be turn on the spit in front of the fire .
` What 's the name of this little stone in the middle of the ocean ? '
ask one of them .
` Ahtola , ' answer the old man .
` Well , you should want for nothing when you live in the Sea King 's dominion . '
Matte do not understand .
He have never read Kalevala and know nothing of the sea god of old , but the student proceed to explain to him .
-LSB- FN # 2 : Kalevala be a collection of old Finnish song about god and hero . -RSB-
` Ahti , ' say they , ` be a mighty king who live in his dominion of Ahtola , and have a rock at the bottom of the sea , and possess besides a treasury of good thing .
He rule over all fish and animal of the deep ; he have the fine cow and the swiftest horse that ever chew grass at the bottom of the ocean .
He who stand well with Ahti be soon a rich man , but one must beware in deal with him , for he be very changeful and touchy .
Even a little stone throw into the water might offend him , and then a he take back his gift , he stir up the sea into a storm and drag the sailor down into the depth .
Ahti own also the fair maiden , who bear the train of his queen Wellamos , and at the sound of music they comb their long , flow lock , which glisten in the water . '
` Oh ! '
cry Matte , ` have your worship really see all that ? '
` We have as good a see it , ' say the student .
` It be all print in a book , and everything print be true . '
` I 'm not so sure of that , ' say Matte , a he shake his head .
But the herring be now ready , and the student eat enough for six , and give Prince some cold meat which they happen to have in the boat .
Prince sit on his hind leg with delight and mew like a pussy cat .
When all be finish , the student hand Matte a shin silver coin , and allow him to fill his pipe with a special kind of tobacco .
They then thank him for his kind hospitality and go on their journey , much regret by Prince , who sit with a woeful expression and whine on the shore as long a he could see a flip of the boat 's white sail in the distance .
Maie have never utter a word , but think the more .
She have good ear , and have lay to heart the story about Ahti .
` How delightful , ' think she to herself , ` to possess a fairy cow !
How delicious every morning and evening to draw milk from it , and yet have no trouble about the feeding , and to keep a shelf near the window for dish of milk and junket !
But this will never be my luck . '
` What be you think of ? '
ask Matte .
` Nothing , ' say his wife ; but all the time she be ponder over some magic rhyme she have heard in her childhood from an old lame man , which be suppose to bring luck in fishing .
` What if I be to try ? '
think she .
Now this be Saturday , and on Saturday evening Matte never set the herring-net , for he do not fish on Sunday .
Towards evening , however , his wife say : ` Let u set the herring-net just this once . '
` No , ' say her husband , ` it be a Saturday night . '
` Last night be so stormy , and we catch so little , ' urge his wife ; ` to-night the sea be like a mirror , and with the wind in this direction the herring be draw towards land . '
` But there be streak in the north-western sky , and Prince be eat grass this evening , ' say the old man .
` Surely he have not eat my garlic , ' exclaim the old woman .
` No ; but there will be rough weather by to-morrow at sunset , ' rejoin Matte .
` Listen to me , ' say his wife , ` we will set only one net close to the shore , and then we shall be able to finish up our half-filled cask , which will spoil if it stand open so long . '
The old man allow himself to be talk over , and so they row out with the net .
When they reach the deep part of the water , she begin to hum the word of the magic rhyme , alter the word to suit the longing of her heart : Oh , Ahti , with the long , long beard , Who dwellest in the deep blue sea , Finest treasure have I hear , And glitter fish belong to thee .
The rich pearls beyond compare Are store up in thy realm below , And Ocean 's cow so sleek and fair Feed on the grass in thy green meadow .
King of the water , far and near , I ask not of thy golden store , I wish not jewel of pearl to wear , Nor silver either , ask I for , But one be odd and even be two , So give me a cow , sea-king so bold , And in return I 'll give to you A slice of the moon , and the sun 's gold .
` What 's that you 're hum ? '
ask the old man .
` Oh , only the word of an old rhyme that keep run in my head , ' answer the old woman ; and she raise her voice and go on : Oh , Ahti , with the long , long beard , Who dwellest in the deep blue sea , A thousand cow be in thy herd , I pray thee give one onto me .
` That 's a stupid sort of song , ' say Matte .
` What else should one beg of the sea-king but fish ?
But such song be not for Sunday . '
His wife pretend not to hear him , and sang and sing the same tune all the time they be on the water .
Matte hear nothing more a he sit and row the heavy boat , while thinking of his crack pipe and the fine tobacco .
Then they return to the island , and soon after go to bed .
But neither Matte nor Maie could sleep a wink ; the one thought of how he have profane Sunday , and the other of Ahti 's cow .
About midnight the fisherman sit up , and say to his wife : ` Dost thou hear anything ? '
` No , ' say she . '
I think the twirling of the weathercock on the roof bodes ill , ' say he ; ` we shall have a storm . '
` Oh , it be nothing but your fancy , ' say his wife .
Matte lay down , but soon rise again .
` The weathercock be squeak now , ' say he .
` Just fancy !
Go to sleep , ' say his wife ; and the old man try to .
For the third time he jump out of bed .
` Ho !
how the weather-cock be roar at the pitch of it voice , a if it have a fire inside it !
We be go to have a tempest , and must bring in the net . '
Both rise .
The summer night be as dark a if it have be October , the weather-cock creak , and the storm be rag in every direction .
As they go out the sea lay around them as white a now , and the spray be dash right over the fisher-hut .
In all his life Matte have never remember such a night .
To launch the boat and put to sea to rescue the net be a thing not to be think of .
The fisherman and his wife stand aghast on the doorstep , hold on fast by the doorpost , while the foam splash over their face .
` Did I not tell thee that there be no luck in Sunday fishing ? '
say Matte sulkily ; and his wife be so frightened that she never even once think of Ahti 's cow .
As there be nothing to be do , they go in .
Their eye be heavy for lack of slumber , and they sleep as soundly a if there have not be such a thing a an angry sea roar furiously around their lonely dwelling .
When they awake , the sun be high in the heaven , the tempest have case , and only the swell of the sea rise in silvery heaving against the red rock .
` What can that be ? '
say the old woman , a she peep out of the door .
` It look like a big seal , ' say Matte .
` As sure a I live , it 's a cow ! '
exclaim Maie .
And certainly it be a cow , a fine red cow , fat and flourishing , and look a if it have be feed all it day on spinach .
It wander peacefully up and down the shore , and never so much a even look at the poor little tuft of grass , a if it despise such fare .
Matte could not believe his eye .
But a cow she seem , and a cow she be find to be ; and when the old woman begin to milk her , every pitcher and pan , even to the baler , be soon fill with the most delicious milk .
The old man trouble his head in vain a to how she come there , and sallied forth to seek for his lost net .
He have not proceed far when he find it cast up on the shore , and so full of fish that not a mesh be visible .
` It be all very fine to possess a cow , ' say Matte , a he clean the fish ; ` but what be we go to fee her on ? '
` We shall find some mean , ' say his wife ; and the cow find the mean herself .
She go out and crop the seaweed which grow in great abundance near the shore , and always keep in good condition .
Every one Prince alone except , think she be a clever beast ; but Prince bark at her , for he have now get a rival .
From that day the red rock overflow with milk and junket , and every net be fill with fish .
Matte and Maie grow fat on this fine living , and daily become rich .
She churn quantity of butter , and he hire two men to help him in his fishing .
The sea lay before him like a big fish tank , out of which he haul as many a he require ; and the cow continue to fend for herself .
In autumn , when Matte and Maie go ashore , the cow go to sea , and in spring , when they return to the rock , there she stand await them .
` We shall require a good house , ' say Maie the following summer ; ` the old one be too small for ourselves and the men . '
` Yes , ' say Matte .
So he build a large cottage , with a real lock to the door , and a store-house for fish as well ; and he and his men catch such quantity of fish that they send ton of salmon , herring , and cod to Russian and Sweden . '
I be quite overwork with so many folk , ' say Maie ; ' a girl to help me would not come amiss . '
` Get one , then , ' say her husband ; and so they hire a girl .
Then Maie say : ` We have too little milk for all these folk .
Now that I have a servant , with the same amount of trouble she could look after three cow . '
` All right , then , ' say her husband , somewhat provoke , ` you can sing a song to the fairy . '
This annoyed Maie , but nevertheless she row out to sea on Sunday night and sang a before : Oh , Ahti , with the long , long beard , Who dwellest in the deep blue sea , A thousand cow be in thy herd , I pray thee give three unto me .
The following morning , instead of one , three cow stand on the island , and they all eat seaweed and fend for themselves like the first one .
` Art thou satisfy now ? '
say Matte to his wife . '
I should be quite satisfied , ' say his wife , ` if only I have two servant to help , and if I have some finer clothes .
Do n't you know that I be address a Madam ? '
` Well , well , ' say her husband .
So Maie get several servant and clothes fit for a great lady .
` Everything would now be perfect if only we have a little well dwell for summer .
You might build u a two-storey house , and fetch soil to make a garden .
Then you might make a little arbour up there to let u have a sea-view ; and we might have a fiddler to fiddle to u of an evening , and a little steamer to take u to church in stormy weather . '
` Anything more ? '
ask Matte ; but he do everything that his wife wish .
The rock Ahtola become so grand and Maie so grand that all the sea-urchins and herring be lose in wonderment .
Even Prince be feed on beefsteak and cream scone till at last he be as round a a butter jar .
` Are you satisfy now ? '
ask Matte . '
I should be quite satisfied , ' say Maie , ` if only I have thirty cow .
At least that number be require for such a household . '
` Go to the fairy , ' say Matte .
His wife set out in the new steamer and sang to the sea-king .
Next morning thirty cow stand on the shore , all finding food for themselves .
` Know ` st thou , good man , that we be far too cramp on this wretched rock , and where be I to find room for so many cow ? '
` There be nothing to be do but to pump out the sea . '
` Rubbish ! '
say his wife .
` Who can pump out the sea ? '
` Try with thy new steamer , there be a pump in it . '
Maie know well that her husband be only make fun of her , but still her mind be set upon the same subject . '
I never could pump the sea out , ' think she , ` but perhaps I might fill it up , if I be to make a big dam .
I might heap up sand and stone , and make our island a big again . '
Maie load her boat with stone and go out to sea .
The fiddler be with her , and fiddle so finely that Ahti and Wellamos and all the sea 's daughter rise to the surface of the water to listen to the music .
` What be that shin so brightly in the wave ? '
ask Maie .
` That be sea foam glinting in the sunshine , ' answer the fiddler .
` Throw out the stone , ' say Maie .
The people in the boat begin to throw out the stone , splash , splash , right and leave , into the foam .
One stone hit the nose of Wellamos 's chief lady-in-waiting , another scratch the sea queen herself on the cheek , a third plumped close to Ahti 's head and tear off half of the sea-king 's beard ; then there be a commotion in the sea , the wave bubble and bubble like boil water in a pot .
` Whence come this gust of wind ? '
say Maie ; and a she speak the sea open and swallow up the steamer .
Maie sink to the bottom like a stone , but , stretch out her arm and leg , she rise to the surface , where she find the fiddler 's fiddle , and use it a a float .
At the same moment she saw close beside her the terrible head of Ahti , and he have only half a beard ! '
` Why do you throw stone at me ? '
roar the sea-king .
` Oh , your majesty , it be a mistake !
Put some bear 's grease on your beard and that will soon make it grow again . '
` Dame , do I not give you all you ask for -- nay , even more ? '
` Truly , truly , your majesty .
Many thanks for the cow . '
` Well , where be the gold from the sun and the silver from the moon that you promise me ? '
` Ah , your majesty , they have be scatter day and night upon the sea , except when the sky be overcast , ' slyly answer Maie .
` I 'll teach you ! '
roar the sea-king ; and with that he give the fiddle such a ` puff ' that it send the old woman up like a sky-rocket on to her island .
There Prince lay , as famish a ever , gnaw the carcase of a crow .
There sat Matte in his ragged grey jacket , quite alone , on the step of the old hut , mend a net .
` Heavens , mother , ' say he , ` where be you come from at such a whirlwind pace , and what make you in such a drip condition ? '
Maie look around her amazed , and say , ` Where be our two-storey house ? '
` What house ? '
ask her husband .
` Our big house , and the flower garden , and the men and the maid , and the thirty beautiful cow , and the steamer , and everything else ? '
` You be talk nonsense , mother , ' say he .
` The student have quite turn your head , for you sing silly song last even while we be row , and then you could not sleep till early morning .
We have stormy weather during the night , and when it be past I do not wish to waken you , so row out alone to rescue the net . '
` But I 've see Ahti , ' rejoin Maie .
` You 've be lie in bed , dream foolish fancy , mother , and then in your sleep you walk into the water . '
` But there be the fiddle , ' say Maie . '
A fine fiddle !
It be only an old stick .
No , no , old woman , another time we will be more careful .
Good luck never attend fish on a Sunday . '
From Z. Topelius .
The Raspberry Worm ` Phew ! '
cry Lisa .
` Ugh ! '
cry Aina .
` What now ? '
cry the big sister . '
A worm ! '
cry Lisa .
` On the raspberry ! '
cry Aina .
` Kill it ! '
cry Otto .
` What a fuss over a poor little worm ! '
say the big sister scornfully .
` Yes , when we have clean the raspberry so carefully , ' say Lisa .
` It creep out from that very large one , ' put in Aina .
` And suppose someone have eat the raspberry , ' say Lisa .
` Then they would have eat the worm , too , ' say Aina .
` Well , what harm ? '
say Otto .
` Eat a worm ! '
cry Lisa .
` And kill him with one bite ! '
murmur Aina .
` Just think of it ! '
say Otto laughing .
` Now it be crawl on the table , ' cry Aina again .
` Blow it away ! '
say the big sister .
` Tramp on it ! '
laugh Otto .
But Lisa take a raspberry leaf , sweep the worm carefully on to the leaf and carry it out into the yard .
Then Aina notice that a sparrow sit on the fence be just ready to pounce on the poor little worm , so she take up the leaf , carry it out into the wood and hide it under a raspberry bush where the greedy sparrow could not find it .
Yes , and what more be there to tell about a raspberry worm ?
Who would give three straw for such a miserable little thing ?
Yes , but who would not like to live in such a pretty home a it live in ; in such a fresh fragrant dark-red cottage , far away in the quiet wood among flower and green leaf !
Now it be just dinner time , so they all have a dinner of raspberry and cream .
` Be careful with the sugar , Otto , ' say the big sister ; but Otto 's plate be like a snowdrift in winter , with just a little red under the snow .
Soon after dinner the big sister say : ` Now we have eat up the raspberry and we have none leave to make preserve for the winter ; it would be fine if we could get two basket full of berry , then we could clean them this evening , and to-morrow we could cook them in the big preserving pan , and then we should have raspberry jam to eat on our bread ! '
` Come , let u go to the wood and pick , ' say Lisa .
` Yes , let u , ' say Aina .
` You take the yellow basket and I will take the green one . '
` Do n't get lose , and come back safely in the evening , ' say the big sister .
` Greetings to the raspberry worm , ' say Otto , mockingly .
` Next time I meet him I shall do him the honour of eat him up . '
So Aina and Lisa go off to the wood .
Ah !
how delightful it be there , how beautiful !
It be certainly tiresome sometimes climb over the fall tree , and get catch in the branch , and wag war with the juniper bush and the midge , but what do that matter ?
The girl climb well in their short dress , and soon they be deep in the wood .
There be plenty of bilberry and elder berry , but no raspberry .
They wander on and on , and at last they come ... No , it could not be true !
... they come to a large raspberry wood .
The wood have be on fire once , and now raspberry bush have grow up , and there be raspberry bush and raspberry bush as far a the eye could see .
Every bush be weight to the ground with the large , dark red , ripe raspberry , such a wealth of berry a two little berry picker have never find before !
Lisa pick , Aina pick .
Lisa ate , Aina ate , and in a little while their basket be full .
` Now we shall go home , ' say Aina .
` No , let u gather a few more , ' say Lisa .
So they put the basket down on the ground and begin to fill their pinafore , and it be not long before their pinafore be full , too .
` Now we shall go home , ' say Lina .
` Yes , now we shall go home , ' say Aina .
Both girl take a basket in one hand and hold up her apron in the other and then turn to go home .
But that be easy say than do .
They have never be so far in the great wood before , they could not find any road nor path , and soon the girl notice that they have lose their way .
The bad of it be that the shadow of the tress be become so long in the evening sunlight , the bird be begin to fly home , and the day be close in .
At last the sun go down behind the pine top , and it be cool and dusky in the great wood .
The girl become anxious but go steadily on , expect that the wood would soon end , and that they would see the smoke from the chimney of their home .
After they have wander on for a long time it begin to grow dark .
At last they reach a great plain overgrown with bush , and when they look around them , they saw , as much a they could in the darkness , that they be among the same beautiful raspberry bush from which they have pick their basket and their apron full .
Then they be so tired that they sit down on a stone and begin to cry . '
I be so hungry , ' say Lisa .
` Yes , ' say Aina , ` if we have only two good meat sandwich now . '
As she say that , she felt something in her hand , and when she look down , she saw a large sandwich of bread and chicken , and at the same time Lisa say : ` How very queer !
I have a sandwich in my hand . '
` And I , too , ' say Aina .
` Will you dare to eat it ? '
` Of course I will , ' say Lisa .
` Ah , if we only have a good glass of milk now ! '
Just a she say that she felt a large glass of milk between her finger , and at the same time Aina cry out , ` Lisa !
Lisa !
I have a glass of milk in my hand !
Is n't it queer ? '
The girl , however , be very hungry , so they eat and drink with a good appetite .
When they have finish Aina yawn , stretch out her arm and say : ` Oh , if only we have a nice soft bed to sleep on now ! '
Scarcely have she speak before she felt a nice soft bed by her side , and there beside Lisa be one too .
This seem to the girl more and more wonderful , but tire and sleepy a they be , they think no more about it , but creep into the little bed , draw the coverlet over their head and be soon asleep .
When they awake the sun be high in the heaven , the wood be beautiful in the summer morning , and the bird be fly about in the branch and the tree top .
At first the girl be fill with wonder when they saw that they have sleep in the wood among the raspberry bush .
They look at each other , they look at their bed , which be of the fine flax cover over with leaf and moss .
At last Lisa say : ` Are you awake , Aina ? '
` Yes , ' say Aina .
` But I be still dream , ' say Lisa .
` No , ' say Aina , ` but there be certainly some good fairy living among these raspberry bush .
Ah , if we have only a hot cup of coffee now , and a nice piece of white bread to dip into it ! '
Scarcely have she finish speak when she saw beside her a little silver tray with a gilt coffee-pot , two cup of rare porcelain , a sugar basin of fine crystal , silver sugar tongs , and some good fresh white bread .
The girl pour out the beautiful coffee , put in the cream and sugar , and taste it ; never in their life have they drink such beautiful coffee .
` Now I should like to know very much who have give u all this , ' say Lisa gratefully . '
I have , my little girl , ' say a voice just then from the bush .
The child look round wonderingly , and saw a little kind-looking old man , in a white coat and a red cap , limp out from among the bush , for he be lame in his left foot ; neither Lisa nor Aina could utter a word , they be so fill with surprise .
` Do n't be afraid , little girl , ' he say smile kindly at them ; he could not laugh properly because his mouth be crook .
` Welcome to my kingdom !
Have you sleep well and eaten well and drink well ? '
he ask .
` Yes , indeed we have , ' say both the girl , ` but tell u ... ' and they want to ask who the old man be , but be afraid to . '
I will tell you who I be , ' say the old man ; ' I be the raspberry king , who reign over all this kingdom of raspberry bush , and I have live here for more than a thousand year .
But the great spirit who rule over the wood , and the sea , and the sky , do not want me to become proud of my royal power and my long life .
Therefore he decree that one day in every hundred year I should change into a little raspberry worm , and live in that weak and helpless form from sunrise to sunset .
During that time my life be dependent on the little worm 's life , so that a bird can eat me , a child can pick me with the berry and trample under foot my thousand year of life .
Now yesterday be just my transformation day , and I be take with the raspberry and would have be trample to death if you have not save my life .
Until sunset I lay helpless in the grass , and when I be sweep away from your table I twist one of my foot , and my mouth become crooked with terror ; but when evening come and I could take my own form again , I look for you to thank you and reward you .
Then I find you both here in my kingdom , and try to meet you both as well a I could without frighten you .
Now I will send a bird from my wood to show you the way home .
Good-bye , little child , thank you for your kind heart ; the raspberry king can show that he be not ungrateful . '
The child shake hand with the old man and thank him , feel very glad that they have save the little raspberry worm .
They be just go when the old man turn round , smile mischievously with his crooked mouth , and say : ` Greetings to Otto from me , and tell him when I meet him again I shall do him the honour of eat him up . '
` Oh , please do n't do that , ' cry both the girl , very frightened .
` Well , for your sake I will forgive him , ' say the old man , ' I be not revengeful .
Greetings to Otto and tell him that he may expect a gift from me , too .
Good-bye . '
The two girl , light of heart , now take their berry and run off through the wood after the bird ; and soon it begin to get lighter in the wood and they wonder how they could have lose their way yesterday , it seem so easy and plain now .
One can imagine what joy there be when the two reach home .
Everyone have be look for them , and the big sister have not be able to sleep , for she think the wolf have eat them up .
Otto meet them ; he have a basket in his hand and say : ` Look , here be something that an old man have just leave for you . '
When the girl look into the basket they saw a pair of most beautiful bracelet of precious stone , dark red , and make in the shape of a ripe raspberry and with an inscription : ` To Lisa and Aina ' ; beside them there be a diamond breast pin in the shape of a raspberry worm : on it be inscribe ` Otto , never destroy the helpless ! '
Otto felt rather ashamed : he quite understand what it mean , but he think that the old man 's revenge be a noble one .
The raspberry king have also remember the big sister , for when she go in to set the table for dinner , she find eleven big basket of most beautiful raspberry , and no one know how they have come there , but everyone guess .
And so there be such a jam-making a have never be see before , and if you like to go and help in it , you might perhaps get a little , for they must surely be make jam still to this very day .
From Z. Topelius .
The Stones of Plouhinec Perhaps some of you may have read a book call ` Kenneth ; or the Rear-Guard of the Grand Army ' of Napoleon .
If so , you will remember how the two Scotch child find in Russia be take care of by the French soldier and prevent as far a possible from suffer from the horror of the terrible Retreat .
One of the soldier , a Breton , often try to make them forget how cold and hungry they be by tell them tale of his native country , Brittany , which be full of wonderful thing .
The best and warm place round the camp fire be always give to the child , but even so the bitter frost would cause them to shiver .
It be then that the Breton would begin : ` Plouhinec be a small town near Hennebonne by the sea , ' and would continue until Kenneth or Effie would interrupt him with an eager question .
Then he forget how his mother have tell him the tale , and be oblige to begin all over again , so the story last a long while , and by the time it be end the child be ready to be roll up in what ever covering could be find , and go to sleep .
It be this story that I be go to tell to you .
Plouhinec be a small town near Hennebonne by the sea .
Around it stretch a desolate moor , where no corn can be grow , and the grass be so coarse that no beast grow fat on it .
Here and there be scattered grove of fir tree , and small pebble be so thick on the ground that you might almost take it for a beach .
On the further side , the fairy , or korigans , a the people call them , have set up long long ago two row of huge stone ; indeed , so tall and heavy be they , that it seem a if all the fairy in the world could not have place them upright .
Not far off them this great stone avenue , and on the bank of the little river Intel , there live a man name Marzinne and his sister Rozennik .
They always have enough black bread to eat , and wooden shoe or sabot to wear , and a pig to fatten , so the neighbour think them quite rich ; and what be still good , they think themselves rich also .
Rozennik be a pretty girl , who know how to make the best of everything , and she could , if she wish , have choose a husband from the young men of Plouhinec , but she care for none of them except Bernez , whom she have play with all her life , and Bernez , though he work hard , be so very very poor that Marzinne tell him roughly he must look elsewhere for a wife .
But whatever Marzinne might say Rozennik smile and nod to him a before , and would often turn her head a she pass , and sing snatch of old song over her shoulder .
Christmas Eve have come , and all the men who work under Marzinne or on the farm round about be gather in the large kitchen to eat the soup flavour with honey follow by rich pudding , to which they be always invite on this particular night .
In the middle of the table be a large wooden bowl , with wooden spoon place in a circle round it , so that each might dip in his turn .
The bench be fill , and Marzinne be about to give the signal , when the door be suddenly thrown open , and an old man come in , wish the guest a good appetite for their supper .
There be a pause , and some of the face look a little frightened ; for the new-comer be well know to them a a beggar , who be also say to be a wizard who cast spell over the cattle , and cause the corn to grow black , and old people to die , of what , nobody know .
Still , it be Christmas Eve , and besides it be as well not to offend him , so the farmer invite him in , and give him a seat at the table and a wooden spoon like the rest .
There be not much talk after the beggar 's entrance , and everyone be glad when the meal come to an end , and the beggar ask if he might sleep in the stable , a he should die of cold if he be leave outside .
Rather unwillingly Marzinne give him leave , and bid Bernez take the key and unlock the door .
There be certainly plenty of room for a dozen beggar , for the only occupant of the stable be an old donkey and a thin ox ; and a the night be bitter , the wizard lay down between them for warmth , with a sack of reed for a pillow .
He have walk far that day , and even wizard get tire sometimes , so in spite of the hard floor he be just drop off to sleep , when midnight struck from the church tower of Plouhinec .
At this sound the donkey raise her head and shake her ear , and turn towards the ox .
` Well , my dear cousin , ' say she , ` and how have you fare since last Christmas Eve , when we have a conversation together ? '
Instead of answer at once , the ox eye the beggar with a long look of disgust .
` What be the use of talk , ' he reply roughly , ` when a good-for-nothing creature like that can hear all we say ? '
` Oh , you must n't lose time in grumble , ' rejoin the donkey gaily , ` and do n't you see that the wizard be asleep ? '
` His wicked prank do not make him rich , certainly , ' say the ox , ` and he be n't even clever enough to have find out what a piece of luck might befall him a week hence . '
` What piece of luck ? '
ask the donkey .
` Why , do n't you know , ' inquire the ox , ` that once very hundred year the stone on Plouhinec heath go down to drink at the river , and that while they be away the treasure underneath them be uncover ? '
` Ah , I remember now , ' reply the donkey , ` but the stone return so quickly to their place , that you certainly would be crush to death unless you have in your hand a bunch of crowsfoot and of five-leaved trefoil . '
` Yes , but that be not enough , ' say the ox ; ` even suppose you get safely by , the treasure you have bring with you will crumble into dust if you do not give in exchange a baptised soul .
It be needful that a Christian should die before you can enjoy the wealth of Plouhinec . '
The donkey be about to ask some further question , when she suddenly find herself unable to speak : the time allow them for conversation be over .
` Ah , my dear creature , ' think the beggar , who have of course heard everything , ` you be go to make me rich than the rich men of Vannes or Lorient .
But I have no time to lose ; to-morrow I must begin to hunt for the precious plant . '
He do not dare to seek too near Plouhinec , l somebody who know the story might guess what he be do , so he go away further towards the south , where the air be soft and the plant be always green .
From the instant it be light , till the last ray have fade out of the sky , he search every inch of ground where the magic plant might grow ; he scarcely give himself a minute to eat and drink , but at length he find the crowsfoot in a little hollow !
Well , that be certainly a great deal , but after all , the crowsfoot be of no use without the trefoil , and there be so little time leave .
He have almost give up hope , when on the very last day before it be necessary that he should start of Plouhinec , he come upon a little clump of trefoil , half hide under a rock .
Hardly able to breathe from excitement , he sit down and hunt eagerly through the plant which he have tear up .
Leaf after leaf he throw aside in disgust , and he have nearly reach the end when he give a cry of joy -- the five-leaved trefoil be in his hand .
The beggar scramble to his foot , and without a pause walk quickly down the road that lead northward .
The moon be bright , and for some hour he keep steadily on , not know how many mile he have go , nor even feeling tire .
By and bye the sun rise , and the world begin to stir , and stop at a farmhouse door , he ask for a cup of milk and slice of bread and permission to rest for a while in the porch .
Then he continue his journey , and so , towards sunset on New Year 's Eve , he come back to Plouhinec .
As he be pass the long line of stone , he saw Bernez work with a chisel on the tallest of them all .
` What be you do there ? '
call the wizard , ` do you mean to hollow out for yourself a bed in that huge column ? '
` No , ' reply Bernez quietly , ` but a I happen to have no work to do to-day , I think I would just carve a cross on this stone .
The holy sign can never come amiss . ' '
I believe you think it will help you to win Rozennik , ' laugh the old man .
Bernez cease his task for a moment to look at him .
` Ah , so you know about that , ' reply he ; ` unluckily Marzinne want a brother-in-law who have more pound than I have penny . '
` And suppose I be to give you more pound than Marzinne ever dream of ? '
whisper the sorcerer glance round to make sure that no one overheard him .
` You ? '
` Yes , I. ' ` And what be I to do to gain the money , ' inquired Bernez , who know quite well that the Breton peasant give nothing for nothing .
` What I want of you only need a little courage , ' answer the old man .
` If that be all , tell me what I have get to do , and I will do it , ' cry Bernez , let fall his chisel .
` If I have to risk thirty death , I be ready . '
When the beggar know that Bernez would give him no trouble , he tell him how , during that very night , the treasure under the stone would be uncover , and how in a very few minute they could take enough to make them both rich for life .
But he keep silence a to the fate that await the man who be without the crowsfoot and the trefoil , and Bernez think that nothing but boldness and quickness be necessary .
So he say : ` Old man , I be grateful , indeed , for the chance you have give me , and there will always be a pint of my blood at your service .
Just let me finish carve this cross .
It be nearly do , and I will join you in the fir wood at whatever hour you please . '
` You must be there without fail an hour before midnight , ' answer the wizard , and go on his way .
As the hour strike from the great church at Plouhinec , Bernez enter the wood .
He find the beggar already there with a bag in each hand , and a third slung round his neck .
` You be punctual , ' say the old man , ` but we need not start just yet .
You have good sit down and think what you will do when your pocket be fill with gold and silver and jewel . '
` Oh , it wo n't take me long to plan out that , ' return Bernez with a laugh . '
I shall give Rozennik everything she can desire , dress of all sort , from cotton to silk , and good thing of all kind to eat , from white bread to orange . '
` The silver you find will pay for all that , and what about the gold ? '
` With the gold I shall make rich Rozennik 's relation and every friend of hers in the parish , ' reply he .
` So much for the gold ; and the jewel ? '
` Then , ' cry Bernez , ' I will divide the jewel amongst everybody in the world , so that they may be wealthy and happy ; and I will tell them that it be Rozennik who would have it so . '
` Hush !
it be close on midnight -- we must go , ' whisper the wizard , and together they creep to the edge of the wood .
With the first stroke of twelve a great noise arose over the silent heath , and the earth seem to rock under the foot of the two watcher .
The next moment by the light of the moon they behold the huge stone near them leave their place and go down the slope lead to the river , knock against each other in their haste .
Passing the spot where stood Bernez and the beggar , they be lose in the darkness .
It seem a if a procession of giant have go by .
` Quick , ' say the wizard , in a low voice , and he rush towards the empty hole , which even in the night shone brightly from the treasure within them .
Flinging himself on his knee , the old man begin fill the wallet he have bring , listen intently all the time for the return of the stone up the hill , while Bernez more slowly put handful of all he could see into his pocket .
The sorcerer have just close his third wallet , and be begin to wonder if he could carry away any more treasure when a low murmur a of a distant storm break upon his ear .
The stone have finish drinking , and be hasten back to their place .
On they come , bend a little forward , the tall of them all at their head , break everything that stand in their way .
At the sight Bernez stand transfixed with horror , and say , ` We be lose !
They will crush u to death . '
` Not me ! '
answer the sorcerer , hold up the crowsfoot and the five-leaved trefoil , ` for these will preserve me .
But in order to keep my rich , I be oblige to sacrifice a Christian to the stone , and an evil fate throw you in my way . '
And a he speak he stretch out the magic herb to the stone , which be advance rapidly .
As if acknowledge a power great than theirs , the monstrous thing instantly part to the right and left of the wizard , but close their rank again a they approach Bernez .
The young man do not try to escape , he know it be useless , and sink on his knee and close his eye .
But suddenly the tall stone that be lead stop straight in front of Bernez , so that no other could get past .
It be the stone on which Bernez have carve the cross , and it be now a baptize stone , and have power to save him .
So the stone remain before the young man till the rest have take their place , and then , dart like a bird to it own hole , come upon the beggar , who , think himself quite safe , be stagger along under the weight of his treasure .
Seeing the stone approaching , he hold out the magic herb which he carry , but the baptized stone be no longer subject to the spell that bind the rest , and pass straight on it way , leave the wizard crush into powder in the heather .
Then Bernez go home , and show his wealth to Marzinne , who this time do not refuse him a a brother-in-law , and he and Rozennik be marry , and live happy for ever after .
From ` Le Royer Breton , ' par Emile Souvestre .
The Castle of Kerglas Peronnik be a poor idiot who belong to nobody , and he would have die of starvation if it have not be for the kindness of the village people , who give him food whenever he choose to ask for it .
And a for a bed , when night come , and he grow sleepy , he look about for a heap of straw , and make a hole in it , creep in , like a lizard .
Idiot though he be , he be never unhappy , but always thank gratefully those who feed him , and sometimes would stop for a little and sing to them .
For he could imitate a lark so well , that no one know which be Peronnik and which be the bird .
He have be wander in a forest one day for several hour , and when even approached , he suddenly felt very hungry .
Luckily , just at that place the tree grow thinner , and he could see a small farmhouse a little way off .
Peronnik go straight towards it , and find the farmer 's wife standing at the door hold in her hand the large bowl out of which her child have eat their supper . '
I be hungry , will you give me something to eat ? '
ask the boy .
` If you can find anything here , you be welcome to it , ' answer she , and , indeed , there be not much left , a everybody 's spoon have dip in .
But Peronnik eat what be there with a hearty appetite , and think that he have never taste good food .
` It be make of the fine flour and mixed with the rich milk and stir by the best cook in all the countryside , ' and though he say it to himself , the woman hear him .
` Poor innocent , ' she murmur , ` he do not know what he be say , but I will cut him a slice of that new wheaten loaf , ' and so she do , and Peronnik eat up every crumb , and declare that nobody less than the bishop 's baker could have bake it .
This flatter the farmer 's wife so much that she give him some butter to spread on it , and Peronnik be still eat it on the doorstep when an arm knight rode up .
` Can you tell me the way to the castle of Kerglas ? '
ask he .
` To Kerglas ?
be you really go to Kerglas ? '
cry the woman , turn pale .
` Yes ; and in order to get there I have come from a country so far off that it have take me three month ' hard rid to travel as far a this . '
` And why do you want to go to Kerglas ? '
say she . '
I be seek the basin of gold and the lance of diamond which be in the castle , ' he answer .
Then Peronnik look up .
` The basin and the lance be very costly thing , ' he say suddenly .
` More costly and precious than all the crown in the world , ' reply the stranger , ` for not only will the basin furnish you with the best food that you can dream of , but if you drink of it , it will cure you of any illness however dangerous , and will even bring the dead back to life , if it touch their mouth .
As to the diamond lance , that will cut through any stone or metal . '
` And to whom do these wonder belong ? '
ask Peronnik in amazement .
` To a magician name Rogear who live in the castle , ' answer the woman .
` Every day he pass along here , mount on a black mare , with a colt thirteen month old trot behind .
But no one dare to attack him , a he always carry his lance . '
` That be true , ' say the knight , ` but there be a spell lay upon him which forbid his use it within the castle of Kerglas .
The moment he enter , the basin and lance be put away in a dark cellar which no key but one can open .
And that be the place where I wish to fight the magician . '
` You will never overcome him , Sir Knight , ' reply the woman , shake her head .
` More than a hundred gentleman have ride past this house bent on the same errand , and not one have ever come back . ' '
I know that , good woman , ' return the knight , ` but then they do not have , like me , instruction from the hermit of Blavet . '
` And what do the hermit tell you ? '
ask Peronnik .
` He tell me that I should have to pass through a wood full of all sort of enchantment and voice , which would try to frighten me and make me lose my way .
Most of those who have go before me have wander they know not where , and perish from cold , hunger , or fatigue . '
` Well , suppose you get through safely ? '
say the idiot .
` If I do , ' continue the knight , ' I shall then meet a sort of fairy arm with a needle of fire which burn to ash all it touch .
This dwarf stand guard an apple-tree , from which I be bound to pluck an apple . '
` And next ? '
inquired Peronnik .
` Next I shall find the flower that laugh , protect by a lion whose mane be form of viper .
I must pluck that flower , and go on to the lake of the dragon and fight the black man who hold in his hand the iron ball which never miss it mark and return of it own accord to it master .
After that , I enter the valley of pleasure , where some who conquer all the other obstacle have leave their bone .
If I can win through this , I shall reach a river with only one ford , where a lady in black will be seat .
She will mount my horse behind me , and tell me what I be to do next . '
He pause , and the woman shake her head .
` You will never be able to do all that , ' say she , but he bid her remembered that these be only matter for men , and gallop away down the path she point out .
The farmer 's wife sigh and , give Peronnik some more food , bid him good-night .
The idiot rise and be open the gate which lead into the forest when the farmer himself come up . '
I want a boy to tend my cattle , ' he say abruptly , ` a the one I have have run away .
Will you stay and do it ? '
and Peronnik , though he love his liberty and hat work , recollect the good food he have eat , and agree to stop .
At sunrise he collect his herd carefully and lead them to the rich pasture which lay along the border of the forest , cut himself a hazel wand with which to keep them in order .
His task be not quite so easy a it look , for the cow have a way of stray into the wood , and by the time he have bring one back another be off .
He have go some distance into the tree , after a naughty black cow which give him more trouble than all the rest , when he hear the noise of horse 's foot , and peep through the leaf he behold the giant Rogear seat on his mare , with the colt trot behind .
Round the giant 's neck hang the golden bowl suspend from a chain , and in his hand he grasp the diamond lance , which gleam like fire .
But as soon a he be out of sight the idiot sought in vain for trace of the path he have take .
This happen not only once but many time , till Peronnik grow so used to him that he never trouble to hide .
But on each occasion he saw him the desire to possess the bowl and the lance become strong .
One even the boy be sit alone on the edge of the forest , when a man with a white beard stop beside him .
` Do you want to know the way to Kerglas ? '
ask the idiot , and the man answer ' I know it well . '
` You have be there without be kill by the magician ? '
cry Peronnik .
` Oh !
he have nothing to fear from me , ' reply the white-bearded man , ' I be Rogear 's elder brother , the wizard Bryak .
When I wish to visit him I always pass this way , and a even I can not go through the enchanted wood without lose myself , I call the colt to guide me . '
Stooping down a he speak he trace three circle on the ground and murmur some word very low , which Peronnik could not hear .
Then he add aloud : Colt , free to run and free to eat .
Colt , gallop fast until we meet , and instantly the colt appear , frisk and jump to the wizard , who throw a halter over his neck and leapt on his back .
Peronnik keep silence at the farm about this adventure , but he understand very well that if he be ever to get to Kerglas he must first catch the colt which know the way .
Unhappily he have not hear the magic word utter by the wizard , and he could not manage to draw the three circle , so if he be to summon the colt at all he must invent some other mean of do it .
All day long , while he be herd the cow , he think and think how he be to call the colt , for he felt sure that once on it back he could overcome the other danger .
Meantime he must be ready in case a chance should come , and he make his preparation at night , when everyone be asleep .
Remembering what he have see the wizard do , he patch up an old halter that be hang in a corner of the stable , twist a rope of hemp to catch the colt 's foot , and a net such a be use for snare bird .
Next he sew roughly together some bit of cloth to serve a a pocket , and this he fill with glue and lark 's feather , a string of bead , a whistle of elder wood , and a slice of bread rub over with bacon fat .
Then he go out to the path down which Rogear , his mare , and the colt always ride , and crumble the bread on one side of it .
Punctual to their hour all three appear , eagerly watch by Peronnik , who lay hid in the bush close by .
Suppose it be useless ; suppose the mare , and not the colt , eat the crumb ?
Suppose -- but no !
the mare and her rider go safely by , vanish round a corner , while the colt , trot along with it head on the ground , smelt the bread , and begin greedily to lick up the piece .
Oh , how good it be !
Why have no one ever give it that before , and so absorbed be the little beast , sniff about after a few more crumb , that it never hear Peronnik creep up till it felt the halter on it neck and the rope round it foot , and -- in another moment -- some one on it back .
Going as fast a the hobble would allow , the colt turn into one of the wild part of the forest , while it rider sit tremble at the strange sight he saw .
Sometimes the earth seem to open in front of them and he be look into a bottomless pit ; sometimes the tree burst into flame and he find himself in the midst of a fire ; often in the act of cross a stream the water rise and threaten to sweep him away ; and again , at the foot of a mountain , great rock would roll towards him , a if they would crush him and his colt beneath their weight .
To his die day Peronnik never know whether these thing be real or if he only imagine them , but he pull down his knitted cap so a to cover his eye , and trust the colt to carry him down the right road .
At last the forest be leave behind , and they come out on a wide plain where the air blow fresh and strong .
The idiot venture to peep out , and find to his relief that the enchantment seem to have end , though a thrill of horror shoot through him a he notice the skeleton of men scatter over the plain , beside the skeleton of their horse .
And what be those grey form trot away in the distance ?
Were they -- could they be -- wolf ?
But vast through the plain seem , it do not take long to cross , and very soon the colt enter a sort of shady park in which be stand a single apple-tree , it branch bow down to the ground with the weight of it fruit .
In front be the korigan -- the little fairy man -- hold in his hand the fiery sword , which reduce to ash everything it touch .
At the sight of Peronnik he utter a piercing scream , and raise his sword , but without appear surprise the youth only lift his cap , though he take care to remain at a little distance .
` Do not be alarm , my prince , ' say Peronnik , ' I be just on my way to Kerglas , a the noble Rogear have beg me to come to him on business . '
` Begged you to come ! '
repeat the dwarf , ` and who , then , be you ? ' '
I be the new servant he have engage , a you know very well , ' answer Peronnik . '
I do not know at all , ' rejoin the korigan sulkily , ` and you may be a robber for all I can tell . ' '
I be so sorry , ' reply Peronnik , ` but I may be wrong in call myself a servant , for I be only a bird-catcher .
But do not delay me , I pray , for his highness the magician expect me , and , a you see , have lend me his colt so that I may reach the castle all the quicker . '
At these word the korigan cast his eye for the first time on the colt , which he know to be the one belonging to the magician , and begin to think that the young man be speak the truth .
After examine the horse , he study the rider , who have such an innocent , and indeed vacant , air that he appear incapable of invent a story .
Still , the dwarf do not feel quite sure that all be right , and ask what the magician want with a bird-catcher .
` From what he say , he want one very badly , ' reply Peronnik , ` a he declare that all his grain and all the fruit in his garden at Kerglas be eat up by the bird . '
` And how be you go to stop that , my fine fellow ? '
inquire the korigan ; and Peronnik show him the snare he have prepare , and remark that no bird could possible escape from it .
` That be just what I should like to be sure of , ' answer the korigan .
` My apple be completely eat up by blackbird and thrush .
Lay your snare , and if you can manage to catch them , I will let you pass . '
` That be a fair bargain , ' and a he speak Peronnik jump down and fasten his colt to a tree ; then , stop , he fix one end of the net to the trunk of the apple tree , and call to the korigan to hold the other while he take out the peg .
The dwarf do a he be bid , when suddenly Peronnik throw the noose over his neck and draw it close , and the korigan be hold as fast a any of the bird he wish to snare .
Shrieking with rage , he try to undo the cord , but he only pull the knot tighter .
He have put down the sword on the grass , and Peronnik have be careful to fix the net on the other side of the tree , so that it be now easy for him to pluck an apple and to mount his horse , without be hinder by the dwarf , whom he leave to his fate .
When they have leave the plain behind them , Peronnik and his steed find themselves in a narrow valley in which be a grove of tree , full of all sort of sweet-smelling thing -- rose of every colour , yellow broom , pink honeysuckle -- while above them all tower a wonderful scarlet pansy whose face bore a strange expression .
This be the flower that laugh , and no one who look at it could help laugh too .
Peronnik 's heart beat high at the thought that he have reach safely the second trial , and he gaze quite calmly at the lion with the mane of viper twist and twirl , who walk up and down in front of the grove .
The young man pull up and remove his cap , for , idiot though he be , he know that when you have to do with people great than yourself , a cap be more useful in the hand than on the head .
Then , after wish all kind of good fortune to the lion and his family , he inquire if he be on the right road to Kerglas .
` And what be your business at Kerglas ? '
ask the lion with a growl , and show his teeth .
` With all respect , ' answer Peronnik , pretend to be very frightened , ' I be the servant of a lady who be a friend of the noble Rogear and send him some lark for a pasty . '
` Larks ? '
cry the lion , lick his long whisker .
` Why , it must be a century since I have have any !
Have you a large quantity with you ? '
` As many a this bag will hold , ' reply Peronnik , opening , a he speak , the bag which he have fill with feather and glue ; and to prove what he say , he turn his back on the lion and begin to imitate the song of a lark .
` Come , ' exclaim the lion , whose mouth water , ` show me the bird !
I should like to see if they be fat enough for my master . ' '
I would do it with pleasure , ' answer the idiot , ` but if I once open the bag they will all fly away . '
` Well , open it wide enough for me to look in , ' say the lion , draw a little nearer .
Now this be just what Peronnik have be hop for , so he hold the bag while the lion open it carefully and put his head right inside , so that he might get a good mouthful of lark .
But the mass of feather and glue stick to him , and before he could pull his head out again Peronnik have draw tight the cord , and tie it in a knot that no man could untie .
Then , quickly gather the flower that laugh , he ride off as fast a the colt could take him .
The path soon lead to the lake of the dragon , which he have to swim across .
The colt , who be accustom to it , plunge into the water without hesitation ; but as soon a the dragon catch sight of Peronnik they approach from all part of the lake in order to devour him .
This time Peronnik do not trouble to take off his cap , but he throw the bead he carry with him into the water , a you throw black corn to a duck , and with each bead that he swallow a dragon turn on his back and die , so that the idiot reach the other side without further trouble .
The valley guard by the black man now lay before him , and from afar Peronnik behold him , chain by one foot to a rock at the entrance , and hold the iron ball which never miss it mark and always return to it master 's hand .
In his head the black man have six eye that be never all shut at once , but keep watch one after the other .
At this moment they be all open , and Peronnik know well that if the black man catch a glimpse of him he would cast his ball .
So , hide the colt behind a thicket of bush , he crawl along a ditch and crouch close to the very rock to which the black man be chain .
The day be hot , and after a while the man begin to grow sleepy .
Two of his eye close , and Peronnik sing gently .
In a moment a third eye shut , and Peronnik sing on .
The lid of a fourth eye drop heavily , and then those of the fifth and the sixth .
The black man be asleep altogether .
Then , on tiptoe , the idiot creep back to the colt which he lead over soft moss past the black man into the vale of pleasure , a delicious garden full of fruit that dangle before your mouth , fountains run with wine , and flower chant in soft little voice .
Further on , table be spread with food , and girl dance on the grass call to him to join them .
Peronnik heard , and , scarcely know what he do draw the colt into a slow pace .
He sniff greedily the smell of the dish , and raise his head the good to see the dancer .
Another instant and he would have stop altogether and be lose , like others before him , when suddenly there come to him like a vision the golden bowl and the diamond lance .
Drawing his whistle from his pocket , he blow it loudly , so a to drown the sweet sound about him , and eat what be leave of his bread and bacon to still the craving of the magic fruit .
His eye he fix steadily on the ear of the colt , that he might not see the dancer .
In this way he be able to reach the end of the garden , and at length perceive the castle of Kerglas , with the river between them which have only one ford .
Would the lady be there , a the old man have tell him ?
Yes , surely that be she , sit on a rock , in a black satin dress , and her face the colour of a Moorish woman 's .
The idiot ride up , and take off his cap more politely than ever , and ask if she do not wish to cross the river . '
I be wait for you to help me do so , ' answer she .
` Come near , that I may get up behind you . '
Peronnik do a she bid him , and by the help of his arm she jump nimbly on to the back of the colt .
` Do you know how to kill the magician ? '
ask the lady , a they be cross the ford . '
I think that , be a magician , he be immortal , and that no one could kill him , ' reply Peronnik .
` Persuade him to taste that apple , and he will die , and if that be not enough I will touch him with my finger , for I be the plague , ' answer she .
` But if I kill him , how be I to get the golden bowl and the diamond lance that be hide in the cellar without a key ? '
rejoin Peronnik .
` The flower that laugh open all door and lighten all darkness , ' say the lady ; and a she speak , they reach the further bank , and advance towards the castle .
In front of the entrance be a sort of tent support on pole , and under it the giant be sit , bask in the sun .
As soon a he notice the colt bearing Peronnik and the lady , he lift his head , and cry in a voice of thunder : ` Why , it be surely the idiot , rid my colt thirteen month old ! '
` Greatest of magician , you be right , ' answer Peronnik .
` And how do you manage to catch him ? '
ask the giant .
` By repeat what I learn from your brother Bryak on the edge of the forest , ' reply the idiot . '
I just say -- Colt , free to run and free to eat , Colt , gallop fast until we meet , and it come directly . '
` You know my brother , then ? '
inquire the giant .
` Tell me why he send you here . '
` To bring you two gift which he have just receive from the country of the Moors , ' answer Peronnik : ` the apple of delight and the woman of submission .
If you eat the apple you will not desire anything else , and if you take the woman a your servant you will never wish for another . '
` Well , give me the apple , and bid the woman get down , ' answer Rogear .
The idiot obey , but at the first taste of the apple the giant stagger , and a the long yellow finger of the woman touch him he fell dead .
Leaving the magician where he lay , Peronnik enter the palace , bear with him the flower that laugh .
Fifty door fly open before him , and at length he reach a long flight of step which seem to lead into the bowel of the earth .
Down these he go till he come to a silver door without a bar or key .
Then he hold up high the flower that laugh , and the door slowly swing back , display a deep cavern , which be as bright a the day from the shining of the golden bowl and the diamond lance .
The idiot hastily run forward and hang the bowl round his neck from the chain which be attach to it , and take the lance in his hand .
As he do so , the ground shake beneath him , and with an awful rumble the palace disappear , and Peronnik find himself stand close to the forest where he lead the cattle to graze .
Though darkness be come on , Peronnik never think of enter the farm , but follow the road which lead to the court of the duke of Brittany .
As he pass through the town of Vannes he stop at a tailor 's shop , and buy a beautiful costume of brown velvet and a white horse , which he pay for with a handful of gold that he have pick up in the corridor of the castle of Kerglas .
Thus he make his way to the city of Nantes , which at that moment be besiege by the French .
A little way off , Peronnik stop and look about him .
For mile round the country be bare , for the enemy have cut down every tree and burnt every blade of corn ; and , idiot though he might be , Peronnik be able to grasp that inside the gate men be die of famine .
He be still gaze with horror , when a trumpeter appear on the wall , and , after blow a loud blast , announce that the duke would adopt a his heir the man who could drive the French out of the country .
On the four side of the city the trumpeter blow his blast , and the last time Peronnik , who have ride up as close a he might , answer him .
` You need blow no more , ' say he , ` for I myself will free the town from her enemy . '
And turn to a soldier who come run up , wave his sword , he touch him with the magic lance , and he fell dead on the spot .
The men who be follow stood still , amaze .
Their comrade 's armour have not be pierce , of that they be sure , yet he be dead , a if he have be strike to the heart .
But before they have time to recover from their astonishment , Peronnik cry out : ` You see how my foe will fare ; now behold what I can do for my friend , ' and , stoop down , he lay the golden bowl against the mouth of the soldier , who sit up as well a ever .
Then , jump his horse across the trench , he enter the gate of the city , which have open wide enough to receive him .
The news of these marvel quickly spread through the town , and put fresh spirit into the garrison , so that they declare themselves able to fight under the command of the young stranger .
And a the bowl restore all the dead Bretons to life , Peronnik soon have an army large enough to drive away the French , and fulfil his promise of deliver his country .
As to the bowl and the lance , no one know what become of them , but some say that Bryak the sorcerer manage to steal them again , and that any one who wish to possess them must seek them a Peronnik do .
From ` Le Foyer Breton , ' par Emile Souvestre .
The Battle of the Birds There be to be a great battle between all the creature of the earth and the bird of the air .
News of it go abroad , and the son of the king of Tethertown say that when the battle be fight he would be there to see it , and would bring back word who be to be king .
But in spite of that , he be almost too late , and every fight have be fight save the last , which be between a snake and a great black raven .
Both struck hard , but in the end the snake prove the strong , and would have twist himself round the neck of the raven till he die have not the king 's son draw his sword , and cut off the head of the snake at a single blow .
And when the raven beheld that his enemy be dead , he be grateful , and say : ` For thy kindness to me this day , I will show thee a sight .
So come up now on the root of my two wing . '
The king 's son do a he be bid , and before the raven stop fly , they have pass over seven ben and seven glen and seven mountain moor .
` Do you see that house yonder ? '
say the raven at last .
` Go straight for it , for a sister of mine dwells there , and she will make you right welcome .
And if she ask , `` Wert thou at the battle of the bird ? ''
answer that thou wert , and if she ask , `` Didst thou see my likeness ? ''
answer that thou sawest it , but be sure thou meet me in the morning at this place . '
The king 's son follow what the raven tell him and that night he have meat of each meat , and drink of each drink , warm water for his foot , and a soft bed to lie in .
Thus it happen the next day , and the next , but on the fourth meeting , instead of meet the raven , in his place the king 's son find wait for him the handsome youth that ever be see , with a bundle in his hand .
` Is there a raven hereabouts ? '
ask the king 's son , and the youth answer : ' I be that raven , and I be deliver by thee from the spell that bind me , and in reward thou wilt get this bundle .
Go back by the road thou camest , and lie a before , a night in each house , but be careful not to unloose the bundle till thou art in the place wherein thou wouldst most wish to dwell . '
Then the king 's son set out , and thus it happen a it have happen before , till he enter a thick wood near his father 's house .
He have walk a long way and suddenly the bundle seem to grow heavy ; first he put it down under a tree , and next he think he would look at it .
The string be easy to untie , and the king 's son soon unfasten the bundle .
What be it he saw there ?
Why , a great castle with an orchard all about it , and in the orchard fruit and flower and bird of very kind .
It be all ready for him to dwell in , but instead of be in the midst of the forest , he do wish he have leave the bundle unloose till he have reach the green valley close to his father 's palace .
Well , it be no use wishing , and with a sigh he glance up , and behold a huge giant come towards him .
` Bad be the place where thou hast build thy house , king 's son , ' say the giant .
` True ; it be not here that I wish to be , ' answer the king 's son .
` What reward wilt thou give me if I put it back in the bundle ? '
ask the giant .
` What reward dost thou ask ? '
answer the king 's son .
` The first boy thou hast when he be seven year old , ' say the giant .
` If I have a boy thou shalt get him , ' answer the king 's son , and a he speak the castle and the orchard be tie up in the bundle again .
` Now take thy road , and I will take mine , ' say the giant .
` And if thou forgettest thy promise , I will remember it . '
Light of heart the king 's son go on his road , till he come to the green valley near his father 's palace .
Slowly he unloose the bundle , fear l he should find nothing but a heap of stone or rag .
But no !
all be a it have be before , and a he open the castle door there stand within the most beautiful maiden that ever be see .
` Enter , king 's son , ' say she , ` all be ready , and we will be marry at once , ' and so they be .
The maiden prove a good wife , and the king 's son , now himself a king , be so happy that he forget all about the giant .
Seven year and a day have go by , when one morning , while stand on the rampart , he behold the giant striding towards the castle .
Then he remember his promise , and remember , too , that he have tell the queen nothing about it .
Now he must tell her , and perhaps she might help him in his trouble .
The queen listen in silence to his tale , and after he have finish , she only say : ` Leave thou the matter between me and the giant , ' and a she speak , the giant enter the hall and stand before them .
` Bring out your son , ' cry he to the king , ` a you promise me seven year and a day since . '
The king glance at his wife , who nod , so he answer : ` Let his mother first put him in order , ' and the queen leave the hall , and take the cook 's son and dress him in the prince 's clothes , and lead him up to the giant , who hold his hand , and together they go out along the road .
They have not walk far when the giant stop and stretch out a stick to the boy .
` If your father have that stick , what would he do with it ? '
ask he .
` If my father have that stick , he would beat the dog and cat that steal the king 's meat , ' reply the boy .
` Thou art the cook 's son ! '
cry the giant .
` Go home to thy mother ' ; and turn his back he stride straight to the castle .
` If you seek to trick me this time , the high stone will soon be the low , ' say he , and the king and queen tremble , but they could not bear to give up their boy .
` The butler 's son be the same age a ours , ' whisper the queen ; ` he will not know the difference , ' and she take the child and dress him in the prince 's clothes , and the giant let him away along the road .
Before they have go far he stop , and hold out a stick .
` If thy father have that rod , what would he do with it ? '
ask the giant .
` He would beat the dog and cat that break the king 's glass , ' answer the boy .
` Thou art the son of the butler ! '
cry the giant .
` Go home to thy mother ' ; and turn round he stride back angrily to the castle .
` Bring out thy son at once , ' roar he , ` or the stone that be high will be low , ' and this time the real prince be bring .
But though his parent weep bitterly and fancy the child be suffer all kind of dreadful thing , the giant treat him like his own son , though he never allow him to see his daughter .
The boy grow to be a big boy , and one day the giant tell him that he would have to amuse himself alone for many hour , a he have a journey to make .
So the boy wander to the top of the castle , where he have never be before .
There he pause , for the sound of music break upon his ear , and open a door near him , he behold a girl sit by the window , hold a harp .
` Haste and begone , I see the giant close at hand , ' she whisper hurriedly , ` but when he be asleep , return hither , for I would speak with thee . '
And the prince do a he be bid , and when midnight strike he creep back to the top of the castle .
` To-morrow , ' say the girl , who be the giant 's daughter , ` to-morrow thou wilt get the choice of my two sister to marry , but thou must answer that thou wilt not take either , but only me .
This will anger him greatly , for he wish to betroth me to the son of the king of the Green City , whom I like not at all . '
Then they part , and on the morrow , a the girl have say , the giant call his three daughter to him , and likewise the young prince to whom he speak .
` Now , O son of the king of Tethertown , the time have come for u to part .
Choose one of my two elder daughter to wife , and thou shalt take her to your father 's house the day after the wedding . '
` Give me the young instead , ' reply the youth , and the giant 's face darken a he hear him .
` Three thing must thou do first , ' say he .
` Say on , I will do them , ' reply the prince , and the giant leave the house , and bid him follow to the byre , where the cow be keep .
