` For a hundred year no man have sweep this byre , ' say the giant , ` but if by nightfall , when I reach home , thou have not clean it so that a golden apple can roll through it from end to end , thy blood shall pay for it . '
All day long the youth toil , but he might as well have try to empty the ocean .
At length , when he be so tired he could hardly move , the giant 's young daughter stand in the doorway .
` Lay down thy weariness , ' say she , and the king 's son , think he could only die once , sink on the floor at her bidding , and fell sound asleep .
When he wake the girl have disappear , and the byre be so clean that a golden apple could roll from end to end of it .
He jump up in surprise , and at that moment in come the giant .
` Hast thou clean the byre , king 's son ? '
ask he . '
I have clean it , ' answer he .
` Well , since thou wert so active to-day , to-morrow thou wilt thatch this byre with a feather from every different bird , or else thy blood shall pay for it , ' and he go out .
Before the sun be up , the youth take his bow and his quiver and set off to kill the bird .
Off to the moor he go , but never a bird be to be see that day .
At last he get so tired with run to and fro that he give up heart .
` There be but one death I can die , ' think he .
Then at midday come the giant 's daughter .
` Thou art tire , king 's son ? '
ask she . '
I be , ' answer he ; ` all these hour have I wander , and there fell but these two blackbird , both of one colour . '
` Lay down thy weariness on the grass , ' say she , and he do a she bid him , and fell fast asleep .
When he wake the girl have disappear , and he get up , and return to the byre .
As he draw near , he rub his eye hard , think he be dream , for there it be , beautifully thatch , just a the giant have wish .
At the door of the house he meet the giant .
` Hast thou thatch the byre , king 's son ? ' '
I have thatch it . '
` Well , since thou hast be so active to-day , I have something else for thee !
Beside the loch thou seest over yonder there grow a fir tree .
On the top of the fir tree be a magpie 's nest , and in the nest be five egg .
Thou wilt bring me those egg for breakfast , and if one be crack or break , thy blood shall pay for it . '
Before it be light next day , the king 's son jump out of bed and run down to the loch .
The tree be not hard to find , for the rise sun shone red on the trunk , which be five hundred foot from the ground to it first branch .
Time after time he walk round it , try to find some knot , however small , where he could put his foot , but the bark be quite smooth , and he soon saw that if he be to reach the top at all , it must be by climb up with his knee like a sailor .
But then he be a king 's son and not a sailor , which make all the difference .
However , it be no use stand there star at the fir , at least he must try to do his best , and try he do till his hand and knee be sore , for as soon a he have struggle up a few foot , he slide back again .
Once he climb a little high than before , and hope rise in his heart , then down he come with such force that his hand and knee smart bad than ever .
` This be no time for stop , ' say the voice of the giant 's daughter , a he lean against the trunk to recover his breath .
` Alas !
I be no sooner up than down , ' answer he .
` Try once more , ' say she , and she lay a finger against the tree and bid him put his foot on it .
Then she place another finger a little high up , and so on till he reach the top , where the magpie have build her nest .
` Make haste now with the nest , ' she cry , ` for my father 's breath be burn my back , ' and down he scramble as fast a he could , but the girl 's little finger have catch in a branch at the top , and she be oblige to leave it there .
But she be too busy to pay heed to this , for the sun be get high over the hill .
` Listen to me , ' she say .
` This night my two sister and I will be dress in the same garment , and you will not know me .
But when my father say ` Go to thy wife , king 's son , ' come to the one whose right hand have no little finger . '
So he go and give the egg to the giant , who nod his head .
` Make ready for thy marriage , ' cry he , ` for the wedding shall take place this very night , and I will summon thy bride to greet thee . '
Then his three daughter be send for , and they all enter dress in green silk of the same fashion , and with golden circlet round their head .
The king 's son look from one to another .
Which be the young ?
Suddenly his eye fell on the hand of the middle one , and there be no little finger .
` Thou hast aim well this time too , ' say the giant , a the king 's son lay his hand on her shoulder , ` but perhaps we may meet some other way ' ; and though he pretend to laugh , the bride saw a gleam in his eye which warn her of danger .
The wedding take place that very night , and the hall be fill with giant and gentleman , and they dance till the house shook from top to bottom .
At last everyone grow tire , and the guest go away , and the king 's son and his bride be leave alone .
` If we stay here till dawn my father will kill thee , ' she whisper , ` but thou art my husband and I will save thee , a I do before , ' and she cut an apple into nine piece , and put two piece at the head of the bed , and two piece at the foot , and two piece at the door of the kitchen , and two at the big door , and one outside the house .
And when this be do , and she hear the giant snoring , she and the king 's son creep out softly and stole across to the stable , where she lead out the blue-grey mare and jump on it back , and her husband mount behind her .
Not long after , the giant awoke .
` Are you asleep ? '
ask he .
` Not yet , ' answer the apple at the head of the bed , and the giant turn over , and soon be snore as loudly a before .
By and bye he call again .
` Are you asleep ? '
` Not yet , ' say the apple at the foot of the bed , and the giant be satisfy .
After a while , he call a third time , ` Are you asleep ? '
` Not yet , ' reply the apple in the kitchen , but when in a few minute , he put the question for the fourth time and receive an answer from the apple outside the house door , he guess what have happen , and run to the room to look for himself .
The bed be cold and empty !
` My father 's breath be burn my back , ' cry the girl , ` put thy hand into the ear of the mare , and whatever thou findest there , throw it behind thee . '
And in the mare 's ear there be a twig of sloe tree , and a he throw it behind him there spring up twenty mile of thornwood so thick that scarce a weasel could go through it .
And the giant , who be stride headlong forward , get catch in it , and it pull his hair and beard .
` This be one of my daughter 's trick , ' he say to himself , ` but if I have my big axe and my wood-knife , I would not be long make a way through this , ' and off he go home and bring back the axe and the wood-knife .
It take him but a short time to cut a road through the blackthorn , and then he lay the axe and the knife under a tree . '
I will leave them there till I return , ' he murmur to himself , but a hoodie crow , which be sit on a branch above , hear him .
` If thou leavest them , ' say the hoodie , ` we will steal them . '
` You will , ' answer the giant , ` and I must take them home . '
So he take them home , and start afresh on his journey .
` My father 's breath be burn my back , ' cry the girl at midday .
` Put thy finger in the mare 's ear and throw behind thee whatever thou findest in it , ' and the king 's son find a splinter of grey stone , and throw it behind him , and in a twinkling twenty mile of solid rock lay between them and the giant .
` My daughter 's trick be the hard thing that ever meet me , ' say the giant , ` but if I have my lever and my crowbar , I would not be long in make my way through this rock also , ' but a he have get them , he have to go home and fetch them .
Then it take him but a short time to hew his way through the rock . '
I will leave the tool here , ' he murmur aloud when he have finish .
` If thou leavest them , we will steal them , ' say a hoodie who be perch on a stone above him , and the giant answer : ` Steal them if thou wilt ; there be no time to go back . '
` My father 's breath be burn my back , ' cry the girl ; ` look in the mare 's ear , king 's son , or we be lose , ' and he look , and find a tiny bladder full of water , which he throw behind him , and it become a great lock .
And the giant , who be stride on so fast , could not stop himself , and he walk right into the middle and be drown .
The blue-grey mare gallop on like the wind , and the next day the king 's son come in sight of his father 's house .
` Get down and go in , ' say the bride , ` and tell them that thou hast marry me .
But take heed that neither man nor beast kiss thee , for then thou wilt cease to remember me at all . ' '
I will do thy bidding , ' answer he , and leave her at the gate .
All who meet him bid him welcome , and he charge his father and mother not to kiss him , but a he greet them his old greyhound leapt on his neck , and kiss him on the mouth .
And after that he do not remember the giant 's daughter .
All that day she sit on a well which be near the gate , wait , wait , but the king 's son never come .
In the darkness she climb up into an oak tree that shadow the well , and there she lay all night , wait , wait .
On the morrow , at midday , the wife of a shoemaker who dwell near the well go to draw water for her husband to drink , and she saw the shadow of the girl in the tree , and think it be her own shadow .
` How handsome I be , to be sure , ' say she , gaze into the well , and a she stop to behold herself good , the jug struck against the stone and break in piece , and she be force to return to her husband without the water , and this anger him .
` Thou hast turn crazy , ' say he in wrath .
` Go thou , my daughter , and fetch me a drink , ' and the girl go , and the same thing befell her a have befall her mother .
` Where be the water ? '
ask the shoemaker , when she come back , and a she hold nothing save the handle of the jug he go to the well himself .
He too saw the reflection of the woman in the tree , but look up to discover whence it come , and there above him sit the most beautiful woman in the world .
` Come down , ' he say , ` for a while thou canst stay in my house , ' and glad enough the girl be to come .
Now the king of the country be about to marry , and the young men about the court throng the shoemaker 's shop to buy fine shoe to wear at the wedding .
` Thou hast a pretty daughter , ' say they when they behold the girl sit at work .
` Pretty she be , ' answer the shoemaker , ` but no daughter of mine . ' '
I would give a hundred pound to marry her , ' say one .
` And I , ' ` And I , ' cry the others .
` That be no business of mine , ' answer the shoemaker , and the young men bid him ask her if she would choose one of them for a husband , and to tell them on the morrow .
Then the shoemaker ask her , and the girl say that she would marry the one who would bring his purse with him .
So the shoemaker hurry to the youth who have first speak , and he come back , and after give the shoemaker a hundred pound for his news , he seek the girl , who be wait for him .
` Is it thou ? '
inquire she . '
I be thirsty , give me a drink from the well that be yonder . '
And he pour out the water , but he could not move from the place where he be ; and there he stay till many hour have pass by .
` Take away that foolish boy , ' cry the girl to the shoemaker at last , ' I be tire of him , ' and then suddenly he be able to walk , and betook himself to his home , but he do not tell the others what have happen to him .
Next day there arrive one of the other young men , and in the evening , when the shoemaker have go out and they be alone , she say to him , ` See if the latch be on the door . '
The young man hasten to do her bidding , but as soon a he touch the latch , his finger stick to it , and there he have to stay for many hour , till the shoemaker come back , and the girl let him go .
Hanging his head , he go home , but he tell no one what have befall him .
Then be the turn of the third man , and his foot remain fasten to the floor , till the girl unloose it .
And thankfully , he run off , and be not see look behind him .
` Take the purse of gold , ' say the girl to the shoemaker , ' I have no need of it , and it will well thee . '
And the shoemaker take it and tell the girl he must carry the shoe for the wed up to the castle . '
I would fain get a sight of the king 's son before he marry , ' sigh she .
` Come with me , then , ' answer he ; ` the servant be all my friend , and they will let you stand in the passage down which the king 's son will pass , and all the company too . '
Up they go to the castle , and when the young men saw the girl stand there , they lead her into the hall where the banquet be lay out and pour her out some wine .
She be just raise the glass to drink when a flame go up out of it , and out of the flame spring two pigeon , one of gold and one of silver .
They fly round and round the head of the girl , when three grain of barley fell on the floor , and the silver pigeon dive down , and swallow them .
` If thou hadst remember how I clean the byre , thou wouldst have give me my share , ' coo the golden pigeon , and a he speak three more grain fell , and the silver pigeon eat them a before .
` If thou hadst remember how I thatch the byre , thou wouldst have give me my share , ' coo the golden pigeon again ; and a he speak three more grain fell , and for the third time they be eat by the silver pigeon .
` If thou hadst remember how I get the magpie 's nest , thou wouldst have give me my share , ' coo the golden pigeon .
Then the king 's son understand that they have come to remind him of what he have forget , and his lost memory come back , and he know his wife , and kiss her .
But a the preparation have be make , it seem a pity to waste them , so they be marry a second time , and sit down to the wedding feast .
From ` Tales of the West Highlands . '
The Lady of the Fountain .
In the centre of the great hall in the castle of Caerleon upon Usk , king Arthur sit on a seat of green rush , over which be thrown a covering of flame-coloured silk , and a cushion of red satin lay under his elbow .
With him be his knight Owen and Kynon and Kai , while at the far end , close to the window , be Guenevere the queen and her maiden embroider white garment with strange device of gold . '
I be weary , ' say Arthur , ` and till my food be prepared I would fain sleep .
You yourselves can tell each other tale , and Kai will fetch you from the kitchen a flagon of mean and some meat . '
And when they have eat and drunk , Kynon , the old among them , begin his story . '
I be the only son of my father and mother , and much store they set by me , but I be not content to stay with them at home , for I think no deed in all the world be too mighty for me .
None could hold me back , and after I have win many adventure in my own land , I bid farewell to my parent and set out to see the world .
Over mountain , through desert , across river I go , till I reach a fair valley full of tree , with a path running by the side of a stream .
I walk along that path all the day , and in the evening I come to a castle in front of which stand two youth clothe in yellow , each grasp an ivory bow , with arrow make of the bone of the whale , and wing with peacock 's feather .
By their side hang golden dagger with hilt of the bone of the whale .
` Near these young men be a man richly dress , who turn and go with me towards the castle , where all the dweller be gather in the hall .
In one window I behold four and twenty damsel , and the least fair of them be fair than Guenevere at her fair .
Some take my horse , and others unbuckle my armour , and wash it , with my sword and spear , till it all shine like silver .
Then I wash myself and put on a vest and doublet which they bring me , and I and the man that enter with me sit down before a table of silver , and a goodlier feast I never have .
` All this time neither the man nor the damsel have speak one word , but when our dinner be half over , and my hunger be still , the man begin to ask who I be .
Then I tell him my name and my father 's name , and why I come there , for indeed I have grow weary of gain the mastery over all men at home , and seek if perchance there be one who could gain the mastery over me .
And at this the man smile and answer : ' `` If I do not fear to distress thee too much , I would show thee what thou seekest . ''
His word make me sorrowful and fearful of myself , which the man perceive , and add , `` If thou mean truly what thou sayest , and desirest earnestly to prove thy valour , and not to boast vainly that none can overcome thee , I have somewhat to show thee .
But to-night thou must sleep in the this castle , and in the morning see that thou rise early and follow the road upwards through the valley , until thou reachest a wood .
In the wood be a path branching to the right ; go along this path until thou comest to a space of grass with a mound in the middle of it .
On the top of the mound stand a black man , large than any two white men ; his eye be in the centre of his forehead and he have only one foot .
He carry a club of iron , and two white men could hardly lift it .
Around him graze a thousand beast , all of different kind , for he be the guardian of that wood , and it be he who will tell thee which way to go in order to find the adventure thou art in quest of . ''
` So spake the man , and long do that night seem to me , and before dawn I rise and put on my armour , and mount my horse and rode on till I reach the grassy space of which he have tell me .
There be the black man on top of the mound , a he have say , and in truth he be mightier in all way than I have think him to be .
As for the club , Kai , it would have be a burden for four of our warrior .
He wait for me to speak , and I ask him what power he hold over the beast that throng so close about him . '
`` I will show thee , little man , '' he answer , and with his club he strike a stag on the head till he bray loudly .
And at his bray the animal come run , numerous a the star in the sky , so that scarce be I able to stand among them .
Serpents be there also , and dragon , and beast of strange shape , with horn in place where never saw I horn before .
And the black man only look at them and bid them go and fee .
And they bow themselves before him , a vassal before their lord . '
`` Now , little man , I have answer thy question and show thee my power , '' say he .
`` Is there anything else thou wouldest know ? ''
Then I inquire of him my way , but he grow angry , and , a I perceive , would fain have hinder me ; but at the last , after I have tell him who I be , his anger pass from him . '
`` Take that path , '' say he , `` that lead to the head of this grassy glade , and go up the wood till thou reachest the top .
There thou wilt find an open space , and in the midst of it a tall tree .
Under the tree be a fountain , and by the fountain a marble slab , and on the slab a bowl of silver , with a silver chain .
Dip the bowl in the fountain , and throw the water on the slab , and thou wilt hear a might peal of thunder , till heaven and earth seem tremble with the noise .
After the thunder will come hail , so fierce that scarcely canst thou endure it and live , for the hailstone be both large and thick .
Then the sun will shine again , but every leaf of the tree will by lie on the ground .
Next a flight of bird will come and alight on the tree , and never didst thou hear a strain so sweet a that which they will sing .
And at the moment in which their song sound sweet thou wilt hear a murmuring and complain come towards thee along the valley , and thou wilt see a knight in black velvet bestride a black horse , bear a lance with a black pennon , and he will spur his steed so a to fight thee .
If thou turnest to flee , he will overtake thee .
And if thou abidest be thou art , he will unhorse thee .
And if thou dost not find trouble in that adventure , thou needest not to seek it during the rest of thy life . ''
` So I bid the black man farewell , and take my way to the top of the wood , and there I find everything just a I have be tell .
I go up to the tree beneath which stand the fountain , and fill the silver bowl with water , empty it on the marble slab .
Thereupon the thunder come , louder by far than I have expect to hear it , and after the thunder come the shower , but heavy by far than I have expect to feel it , for , of a truth I tell thee , Kai , not one of those hailstone would be stop by skin or by flesh till it have reach the bone .
I turn my horse 's flank towards the shower , and , bend over his neck , hold my shield so that it might cover his head and my own .
When the hail have pass , I look on the tree and not a single leaf be leave on it , and the sky be blue and the sun shining , while on the branch be perch bird of very kind , who sing a song sweeter than any that have come to my ear , either before or since .
` Thus , Kai , I stand listen to the bird , when lo , a murmuring voice approach me , say : ' `` O knight , what have bring thee hither ?
What evil have I do to thee , that thou shouldest do so much to me , for in all my land neither man nor beast that meet that shower have escape alive . ''
Then from the valley appear the knight on the black horse , grasp the lance with the black pennon .
Straightway we charge each other , and though I fight my best , he soon overcame me , and I be throw to the ground , while the knight seize the bridle of my horse , and ride away with it , leave me where I be , without even despoil me of my armour .
` Sadly do I go down the hill again , and when I reach the glade where the black man be , I confess to thee , Kai , it be a marvel that I do not melt into a liquid pool , so great be my shame .
That night I sleep at the castle where I have be before , and I be bath and feast , and none ask me how I have fare .
The next morning when I arise I find a bay horse saddle for me , and , girdle on my armour , I return to my own court .
The horse be still in the stable , and I would not part with it for any in Britain .
` But of a truth , Kai , no man ever confess an adventure so much to his own dishonour , and strange indeed it seem that none other man have I ever meet that knew of the black man , and the knight and the shower . '
` Would it not be well , ' say Owen , ` to go and discover the place ? '
` By the hand of my friend , ' answer Kai , ` often dost thou utter that with thy tongue which thou wouldest not make good with thy deed . '
` In truth , ' say Guenevere the queen , who have listen to the tale , ` thou wert well hang , Kai , than use such speech towards a man like Owen . ' '
I mean nothing , lady , ' reply Kai ; ` thy praise of Owen be not great than mine . '
And a he speak Arthur awoke , and ask if he have not sleep for a little .
` Yes , lord , ' answer Owen , ` certainly thou hast slept . '
` Is it time for u to go to meat ? '
` It be , lord , ' answer Owen .
Then the horn for wash themselves be sound , and after that the king and his household sit down to eat .
And when they have finish , Owen leave them , and make ready his horse and his arm .
With the first ray of the sun he set forth , and travel through desert and over mountain and across river , and all befall him which have befall Kynon , till he stand under the leafless tree listen to the song of the bird .
Then he hear the voice , and turn to look found the knight gallop to meet him .
Fiercely they fight till their lance be break , and then they draw their sword , and a blow from Owen cut through the knight 's helmet , and pierce his skull .
Feeling himself wound unto death the knight flee , and Owen pursue him till they come to a splendid castle .
Here the knight dash across the bridge that span the moat , and enter the gate , but as soon a he be safe inside , the drawbridge be pull up and catch Owen 's horse in the middle , so that half of him be inside and half out , and Owen could not dismount and know not what to do .
While he be in this sore plight a little door in the castle gate open , and he could see a street face him , with tall house .
Then a maiden with curl hair of gold look through the little door and bade Owen open the gate .
` By my troth ! '
cry Owen , ' I can no more open it from here than thou art able to set me free . '
` Well , ' say she , ' I will do my best to release thee if thou wilt do a I tell thee .
Take this ring and put it on with the stone inside thy hand , and close thy finger tight , for as long a thou dost conceal it , it will conceal thee .
When the men inside have hold counsel together , they will come to fetch thee to thy death , and they will be much grieve not to find thee .
I will stand on the horse block yonder and thou canst see me though I can not see thee .
Therefore draw near and place thy hand on my shoulder and follow me wheresoever I go . '
Upon that she go away from Owen , and when the men come out from the castle to seek him and do not find him they be sorely grieve , and they return to the castle .
Then Owen go to the maiden and place his hand on her shoulder , and she guide him to a large room , paint all over with rich colour , and adorn with image of gold .
Here she give him meat and drink , and water to wash with and garment to wear , and he lay down upon a soft bed , with scarlet and fur to cover him , and sleep gladly .
In the middle of the night he wake hear a great outcry , and he jump up and clothe himself and go into the hall , where the maiden be stand .
` What be it ? '
he ask , and she answer that the knight who own the castle be dead , and they be bear his body to the church .
Never have Owen behold such vast crowd , and follow the dead knight be the most beautiful lady in the world , whose cry be loud than the shout of the men , or the braying of the trumpet .
And Owen look on her and love her .
` Who be she ? '
he ask the damsel .
` That be my mistress , the countess of the fountain , and the wife of him whom thou didst slay yesterday . '
` Verily , ' say Owen , ` she be the woman that I love best . '
` She shall also love thee not a little , ' say the maiden .
Then she leave Owen , and after a while go into the chamber of her mistress , and speak to her , but the countess answer her nothing .
` What aileth thee , mistress ? '
inquire the maiden .
` Why hast thou keep far from me in my grief , Luned ? '
answer the countess , and in her turn the damsel ask : ` Is it well for thee to mourn so bitterly for the dead , or for anything that be go from thee ? '
` There be no man in the world equal to him , ' reply the countess , her cheek grow red with anger . '
I would fain banish thee for such word . '
` Be not angry , lady , ' say Luned , ` but listen to my counsel .
Thou knowest well that alone thou canst not preserve thy land , therefore seek some one to help thee . '
` And how can I do that ? '
ask the countess . '
I will tell thee , ' answer Luned .
` Unless thou canst defend the fountain all will be lose , and none can defend the fountain except a knight of Arthur 's court .
There will I go to seek him , and woe betide me if I return without a warrior that can guard the fountain , as well a he who keep it before . '
` Go then , ' say the countess , ` and make proof of that which thou hast promise . '
So Luned set out , rid on a white palfrey , on pretence of journey to King Arthur 's court , but instead of do that she hide herself for as many day a it would have take her to go and come , and then she leave her hiding-place , and go into the countess .
` What news from the court ? '
ask her mistress , when she have give Luned a warm greeting .
` The best of news , ' answer the maiden , ` for I have gain the object of my mission .
When wilt thou that I present to thee the knight who have return with me ? '
` To-morrow at midday , ' say the countess , ` and I will cause all the people in the town to come together . '
Therefore the next day at noon Owen put on his coat of mail , and over it he wear a splendid mantle , while on his foot be leather shoe fasten with clasp of gold .
And he follow Luned to the chamber of her mistress .
Right glad be the countess to see them , but she look closely at Owen and say : ` Luned , this knight have scarcely the air of a traveller . '
` What harm be there in that , lady ? '
answer Luned . '
I be persuade , ' say the countess , ` that this man and no other chase the soul from the body of my lord . '
` Had he not be strong than thy lord , ' reply the damsel , ` he could not have take his life , and for that , and for all thing that be past , there be no remedy . '
` Leave me , both of you , ' say the countess , ` and I will take counsel . '
Then they go out .
The next morning the countess summon her subject to meet in the courtyard of the castle , and tell them that now that her husband be dead there be none to defend her land .
` So choose you which it shall be , ' she say .
` Either let one of you take me for a wife , or give me your consent to take a new lord for myself , that my land be not without a master . '
At her word the chief men of the city withdraw into one corner and take counsel together , and after a while the leader come forward and say that they have decide that it be best , for the peace and safety of all , that she should choose a husband for herself .
Thereupon Owen be summon to her presence , and he accept with joy the hand that she offer him , and they be marry forthwith , and the men of the earldom do him homage .
From that day Owen defend the fountain a the earl before him have do , and every knight that come by be overthrow by him , and his ransom divide among his baron .
In this way three year pass , and no man in the world be more beloved than Owen .
Now at the end of the three year it happen that Gwalchmai the knight be with Arthur , and he perceive the king to be very sad .
` My lord , have anything befall thee ? '
he ask .
` Oh , Gwalchmai , I be grieved concerning Owen , whom I have lose these three year , and if a fourth year pass without him I can live no longer .
And sure be I that the tale tell by Kynon the son of Clydno cause me to lose him .
I will go myself with the men of my household to avenge him if he be dead , to free him if he be in prison , to bring him back if he be alive . '
Then Arthur and three thousand men of his household set out in quest of Owen , and take Kynon for their guide .
When Arthur reach the castle , the youth be shoot in the same place , and the same yellow man be stand by , and as soon a he behold Arthur he greet him and invite him in , and they enter together .
So vast be the castle that the king 's three thousand men be of no more account than if they have be twenty .
At sunrise Arthur depart thence , with Kynon for his guide , and reach the black man first , and afterwards the top of the wooded hill , with the fountain and the bowl and the tree .
` My lord , ' say Kai , ` let me throw the water on the slab , and receive the first adventure that may befall . '
` Thou mayest do so , ' answer Arthur , and Kai throw the water .
Immediately all happen a before ; the thunder and the shower of hail which kill many of Arthur 's men ; the song of the bird and the appearance of the black knight .
And Kai meet him and fight him , and be overthrow by him .
Then the knight ride away , and Arthur and his men encamp where they stand .
In the morning Kai again ask leave to meet the knight and to try to overcome him , which Arthur grant .
But once more he be unhorsed , and the black knight 's lance break his helmet and pierce the skin even to the bone , and humble in spirit he return to the camp .
After this every one of the knight give battle , but none come out victor , and at length there only remain Arthur himself and Gwalchmai .
` Oh , let me fight him , my lord , ' cry Gwalchmai , a he saw Arthur take up his arm .
` Well , fight then , ' answer Arthur , and Gwalchmai throw a robe over himself and his horse , so that none know him .
All that day they fight , and neither be able to throw the other , and so it be on the next day .
On the third day the combat be so fierce that they fell both to the ground at once , and fought on their foot , and at last the black knight give his foe such a blow on his head that his helmet fell from his face . '
I do not know it be thee , Gwalchmai , ' say the black knight .
` Take my sword and my arm . '
` No , ' answer Gwalchmai , ` it be thou , Owen , who art the victor , take thou my sword ' ; but Owen would not .
` Give me your sword , ' say Arthur from behind them , ` for neither of you have vanquish the other , ' and Owen turn and put his arm round Arthur 's neck .
The next day Arthur would have give order to his men to make ready to go back whence they come , but Owen stop him .
` My lord , ' he say , ` during the three year that I have be absent from thee I have be prepare a banquet for thee , know full well that thou wouldst come to seek me .
Tarry with me , therefore , for a while , thou and thy men . '
So they ride to the castle of the countess of the fountain , and spend three month in rest and feasting .
And when it be time for them to depart Arthur beseech the countess that she would allow Owen to go with him to Britain for the space of three month .
With a sore heart she grant permission , and so content be Owen to be once more with his old companion that three year instead of three month pass away like a dream .
One day Owen sit at meat in the castle of Caerleon upon Usk , when a damsel on a bay horse enter the hall , and rid straight up to the place where Owen sit she stoop and draw the ring from off his hand .
` Thus shall be treat the traitor and the faithless , ' say she , and turn her horse 's head she ride out of the hall .
At her word Owen remember all that he have forget , and sorrowful and ashamed he go to his own chamber and make ready to depart .
At the dawn he set out , but he do not go back to the castle , for his heart be heavy , but he wander far into wild place till his body be weak and thin , and his hair be long .
The wild beast be his friend , and he slept by their side , but in the end he long to see the face of a man again , and he come down into a valley and fell asleep by a lake in the land of a widowed countess .
Now it be the time when the countess take her walk , attend by her maiden , and when they saw a man lying by the lake they shrink back in terror , for he lay so still that they think he be dead .
But when they have overcome their fright , they draw near him , and touch him , and saw that there be life in him .
Then the countess hasten to the castle , and bring from it a flask full of precious ointment and give it to one of her maiden .
` Take that horse which be graze yonder , ' she say , ` and a suit of men 's garment , and place them near the man , and pour some of this ointment near his heart .
If there be any life in him that will bring it back .
But if he move , hide thyself in the bush near by , and see what he do . '
The damsel take the flask and do her mistress ' bidding .
Soon the man begin to move his arm , and then rise slowly to his foot .
Creeping forward step by step he take the garment from off the saddle and put them on him , and painfully he mount the horse .
When he be seat the damsel come forth and greet him , and glad be he when he saw her and inquire what castle that be before him .
` It belong to a widowed countess , ' answer the maiden .
` Her husband leave her two earldom , but it be all that remain of her broad land , for they have be tear from her by a young earl , because she would not marry him . '
` That be a pity , ' reply Owen , but he say no more , for he be too weak to talk much .
Then the maiden guide him to the castle , and kindle a fire , and bring him food .
And there he stay and be tend for three month , till he be handsome than ever he be .
At noon one day Owen hear a sound of arm outside the castle , and he ask of the maiden what it be .
` It be the earl of whom I speak to thee , ' she answer , ` who have come with a great host to carry off my mistress . '
` Beg of her to lend me a horse and armour , ' say Owen , and the maiden do so , but the countess laugh somewhat bitterly a she answer : ` Nay , but I will give them to him , and such a horse and armour and weapon a he have never have yet , though I know not what use they will be to him .
Yet mayhap it will save them from fall into the hand of my enemy . '
The horse be bring out and Owen ride forth with two page behind him , and they saw the great host encamp before them .
` Where be the earl ? '
say he , and the page answer : ` In yonder troop where be four yellow standard . '
` Await me , ' say Owen , ` at the gate of the castle , and he cry a challenge to the earl , who come to meet him .
Hard do they fight , but Owen overthrow his enemy and drive him in front to the castle gate and into the hall .
` Behold the reward of thy bless balsam , ' say he , a he bid the earl kneel down before her , and make him swear that he would restore all that he have take from her .
After that he depart , and go into the desert , and a he be pass through a wood he hear a loud yelling .
Pushing aside the bush he behold a lion stand on a great mound , and by it a rock .
Near the rock be a lion seek to reach the mound , and each time he move out dart a serpent from the rock to prevent him .
Then Owen unsheathe his sword , and cut off the serpent 's head and go on his way , and the lion follow and play about him , a if he have be a greyhound .
And much more useful be he than a greyhound , for in the evening he bring large log in his mouth to kindle a fire , and kill a fat buck for dinner .
Owen make his fire and skin the buck , and put some of it to roast , and give the rest to the lion for supper .
While he be wait for the meat to cook he hear a sound of deep sigh close to him , and he say : ` Who be thou ? ' '
I be Luned , ' reply a voice from a cave so hidden by bush and green hanging plant that Owen have not see it .
` And what dost thou here ? '
cry he . '
I be hold captive in this cave on account of the knight who marry the countess and leave her , for the page speak ill of him , and because I tell them that no man living be his equal they drag me here and say I should die unless he should come to deliver me by a certain day , and that be no further than the day after to-morrow .
His name be Owen the son of Urien , but I have none to send to tell him of my danger , or of a surety he would deliver me . '
Owen hold his peace , but give the maiden some of the meat , and bid her be of good cheer .
Then , follow by the lion , he set out for a great castle on the other side of the plain , and men come and take his horse and place it in a manger , and the lion go after and lay down on the straw .
Hospitable and kind be all within the castle , but so full of sorrow that it might have be think death be upon them .
At length , when they have eat and drunk , Owen pray the earl to tell him the reason of their grief .
` Yesterday , ' answer the earl , ` my two son be seize , while thy be hunt , by a monster who dwell on those mountain yonder , and he vow that he will not let them go unless I give him my daughter to wife . '
` That shall never be , ' say Owen ; ` but what form hath this monster ? '
` In shape he be a man , but in stature he be a giant , ' reply the earl , ` and it be good by far that he should slay my son than that I should give up my daughter . '
Early next morning the dweller in the castle be awaken by a great clamour , and they find that the giant have arrive with the two young men .
Swiftly Owen put on his armour and go forth to meet the giant , and the lion follow at his heel .
And when the great beast behold the hard blow which the giant deal his master he fly at his throat , and much trouble have the monster in beat him off .
` Truly , ' say the giant , ' I should find no difficulty in fight thee , if it be not for that lion . '
When he hear that Owen felt shame that he could not overcome the giant with his own sword , so he take the lion and shut him up in one of the tower of the castle , and return to the fight .
But from the sound of the blow the lion know that the combat be go ill for Owen , so he climb up till he reach the top of the tower , where there be a door on to the roof , and from the tower he spring on to the wall , and from the wall to the ground .
Then with a loud roar he leap upon the giant , who fell dead under the blow of his paw .
Now the gloom of the castle be turn into rejoicing , and the earl beg Owen to stay with him till he could make him a feast , but the knight say he have other work to do , and ride back to the place where he have leave Luned , and the lion follow at his heel .
When he come there he saw a great fire kindle , and two youth lead out the maiden to cast her upon the pile .
` Stop ! '
he cry , dash up to them .
` What charge have you against her ? '
` She boast that no man in the world be equal to Owen , ' say they , ` and we shut her in a cave , and agree that none should deliver her but Owen himself , and that if he do not come by a certain day she should die .
And now the time have past and there be no sign of him . '
` In truth he be a good knight , and have he but know that the maid be in peril he would have come to save her , ' say Owen ; ` but accept me in his stead , I entreat you . '
` We will , ' reply they , and the fight begin .
The youth fight well and press hard on Owen , and when the lion saw that he come to help his master .
But the youth make a sign for the fight to stop , and say : ` Chieftain , it be agree we should give battle to thee alone , and it be hard for u to contend with yonder beast than with thee . '
Then Owen shut up the lion in the cave where the maiden have be in prison , and block up the front with stone .
But the fight with the giant have sorely try him , and the youth fought well , and press him hard than before .
And when the lion saw that he give a loud roar , and burst through the stone , and spring upon the youth and slew them .
And so Luned be deliver at the last .
Then the maiden rode back with Owen to the land of the lady of the fountain .
And he take the lady with him to Arthur 's court , where they live happily till they die .
From the ` Mabinogion . '
The Four Gifts In the old land of Brittany , once call Cornwall , there live a woman name Barbaik Bourhis , who spend all her day in look after her farm with the help of her niece Tephany .
Early and late the two might be see in the field or in the dairy , milk cow , make butter , feed fowl ; work hard themselves and take care that others work too .
Perhaps it might have be good for Barbaik if she have leave herself a little time to rest and to think about other thing , for soon she grow to love money for it own sake , and only give herself and Tephany the food and clothes they absolutely need .
And a for poor people she positively hat them , and declare that such lazy creature have no business in the world .
Well , this be the sort of person Barbaik be , it be easy to guess at her anger when one day she find Tephany talk outside the cowhouse to young Denis , who be nothing more than a day labourer from the village of Plover .
Seizing her niece by the arm , she pull her sharply away , exclaim : ` Are you not ashamed , girl , to waste your time over a man who be as poor a a rat , when there be a dozen more who would be only too happy to buy you ring of silver , if you would let them ? '
` Denis be a good workman , a you know very well , ' answer Tephany , red with anger , ` and he put by money too , and soon he will be able to take a farm for himself . '
` Nonsense , ' cry Barbaik , ` he will never save enough for a farm till he be a hundred .
I would sooner see you in your grave than the wife of a man who carry his whole fortune on his back . '
` What do fortune matter when one be young and strong ? '
ask Tephany , but her aunt , amaze at such word , would hardly let her finish .
` What do fortune matter ? '
repeat Barbaik , in a shocked voice .
` Is it possible that you be really so foolish a to despise money ?
If this be what you learn from Denis , I forbid you to speak to him , and I will have him turn out of the farm if he dare to show his face here again .
Now go and wash the clothes and spread them out to dry . '
Tephany do not dare to disobey , but with a heavy heart go down the path to the river .
` She be hard than these rock , ' say the girl to herself , ` yes , a thousand time hard .
For the rain at least can at last wear away the stone , but you might cry for ever , and she would never care .
Talking to Denis be the only pleasure I have , and if I be not to see him I may as well enter a convent . '
Thinking these thought she reach the bank , and begin to unfold the large packet of linen that have to be wash .
The tap of a stick make her look up , and stand before her she saw a little old woman , whose face be strange to her .
` You would like to sit down and rest , granny ? '
ask Tephany , push aside her bundle .
` When the sky be all the roof you have , you rest where you will , ' reply the old woman in tremble tone .
` Are you so lonely , then ? '
inquire Tephany , full of pity .
` Have you no friend who would welcome you into their house ? '
The old woman shake her head .
` They all die long , long ago , ' she answer , ` and the only friend I have be stranger with kind heart . '
The girl do not speak for a moment , then hold out the small loaf and some bacon intend for her dinner .
` Take this , ' she say ; ` to-day at any rate you shall dine well , ' and the old woman take it , gaze at Tephany the while .
` Those who help others deserve to be help , ' she answer ; ` your eye be still red because that miser Barbaik have forbid you to speak to the young man from Plover .
But cheer up , you be a good girl , and I will give you something that will enable you to see him once every day . '
` You ? '
cry Tephany , stupefy at discover that the beggar know all about her affair , but the old woman do not hear her .
` Take this long copper pin , ' she go on , ` and every time you stick it in your dress Mother Bourhis will be oblige to leave the house in order to go and count her cabbage .
As long a the pin be in your dress you will be free , and your aunt will not come back until you have put it in it case again . '
Then , rise , she nod to Tephany and vanish .
The girl stand where she be , as still a a stone .
If it have not be for the pin in her hand she would have think she be dream .
But by that token she know it be no common old woman who have give it to her , but a fairy , wise in tell what would happen in the day to come .
Then suddenly Tephany 's eye fell on the clothes , and to make up for lose time she begin to wash them with great vigour .
Next evening , at the moment when Denis be accustom to wait for her in the shadow of the cowhouse , Tephany stick the pin in her dress , and at the very same instant Barbaik take up her sabot or wooden shoe and go through the orchard and past to the field , to the plot where the cabbage grow .
With a heart as light a her footstep , the girl run from the house , and spend her even happily with Denis .
And so it be for many day after that .
Then , at last , Tephany begin to notice something , and the something make her very sad .
At first , Denis seem to find the hour that they be together fly as quickly a she do , but when he have teach her all the song he know , and tell her all the plan he have make for grow rich and a great man , he have nothing more to say to her , for he , like a great many other people , be fond of talk himself , but not of listen to any one else .
Sometimes , indeed , he never come at all , and the next evening he would tell Tephany that he have be force to go into the town on business , but though she never reproach him she be not deceive and saw plainly that he no longer care for her a he use to do .
Day by day her heart grow heavy and her cheek paler , and one evening , when she have wait for him in vain , she put her water-pot on her shoulder and go slowly down to the spring .
On the path in front of her stood the fairy who have give her the pin , and a she glance at Tephany she give a little mischievous laugh and say : ` Why , my pretty maiden hardly look happy than she do before , in spite of meet her lover whenever she please . '
` He have grow tire of me , ' answer Tephany in a trembling voice , ` and he make excuse to stay away .
Ah !
granny dear , it be not enough to be able to see him , I must be able to amuse him and to keep him with me .
He be so clever , you know .
Help me to be clever too . '
` Is that what you want ? '
cry the old woman .
` Well , take this feather and stick it in your hair , and you will be as wise a Solomon himself . '
Blushing with pleasure Tephany go home and stick the feather into the blue ribbon which girls always wear in that part of the country .
In a moment she hear Denis whistle gaily , and a her aunt be safely count her cabbage , she hurry out to meet him .
The young man be strike dumb by her talk .
There be nothing that she do not seem to know , and a for song she not only could sing those from every part of Brittany , but could compose them herself .
Was this really the quiet girl who have be so anxious to learn all he could teach her , or be it somebody else ?
Perhaps she have go suddenly mad , and there be an evil spirit inside her .
But in any case , night after night he come back , only to find her grow wiser and wiser .
Soon the neighbour whisper their surprise among themselves , for Tephany have not be able to resist the pleasure of put the feather in her hair for some of the people who despise her for her poor clothes , and many be the joke she make about them .
Of course they hear of her jest , and shake their head say : ` She be an ill-natured little cat , and the man that marry her will find that it be she who will hold the rein and drive the horse . '
It be not long before Denis begin to agree with them , and a he always like to be master wherever he go , he become afraid of Tephany 's sharp tongue , and instead of laugh a before when she make fun of other people he grow red and uncomfortable , think that his turn would come next .
So matter go on till one evening Denis tell Tephany that he really could not stay a moment , a he have promise to go to a dance that be to be hold in the next village .
Tephany 's face fell ; she have work hard all day , and have be count on a quiet hour with Denis .
She do her best to persuade him to remain with her , but he would not listen , and at last she grow angry .
` Oh , I know why you be so anxious not to miss the dance , ' she say ; ` it be because Aziliez of Pennenru will be there . '
Now Aziliez be the lovely girl for mile round , and she and Denis have know each other from childhood .
` Oh yes , Aziliez will be there , ' answer Denis , who be quite pleased to see her jealous , ` and naturally one would go a long way to watch her dance . '
` Go then ! '
cry Tephany , and enter the house she slam the door behind her .
Lonely and miserable she sit down by the fire and star into the red ember .
Then , fling the feather from her hair , she put her head on her hand , and sob passionately .
` What be the use of be clever when it be beauty that men want ?
That be what I ought to have ask for .
But it be too late , Denis will never come back . '
` Since you wish it so much you shall have beauty , ' say a voice at her side , and look round she behold the old woman lean on her stick .
` Fasten this necklace round your neck , and as long a you wear it you will be the most beautiful woman in the world , ' continue the fairy .
With a little shriek of joy Tephany take the necklace , and snap the clasp run to the mirror which hung in the corner .
Ah , this time she be not afraid of Aziliez or of any other girl , for surely none could be a fair and white a she .
And with the sight of her face a thought come to her , and put on hastily her best dress and her buckled shoe she hurry off to the dance .
On the way she meet a beautiful carriage with a young man seat in it .
` What a lovely maiden ! '
he exclaim , a Tephany approach .
` Why , there be not a girl in my own country that can be compare to her .
She , and no other , shall be my bride . '
The carriage be large and bar the narrow road , so Tephany be force , much against her will , to remain where she be .
But she look the young man full in the face a she answer : ` Go your way , noble lord , and let me go mine .
I be only a poor peasant girl , accustom to milk , and make hay and spin . '
` Peasant you may be , but I will make you a great lady , ' say he , take her hand and try to lead her to the carriage . '
I do n't want to be a great lady , I only want to be the wife of Denis , ' she reply , throw off his hand and running to the ditch which divide the road from the cornfield , where he hop to hide .
Unluckily the young man guess what she be do , and sign to his attendant , who seize her and put her in the coach .
The door be bang , and the horse whip up into a gallop .
At the end of an hour they arrive at a splendid castle , and Tephany , who would not move , be lift out and carry into the hall , while a priest be send for to perform the marriage ceremony .
The young man try to win a smile from her by tell of all the beautiful thing she should have a his wife , but Tephany do not listen to him , and look about to see if there be any mean by which she could escape .
It do not seem easy .
The three great door be closely bar , and the one through which she have enter shut with a spring , but her feather be still in her hair , and by it aid she detect a crack in the wooden panelling , through which a streak of light could be dimly see .
Touching the copper pin which fasten her dress , the girl send every one in the hall to count the cabbage , while she herself pass through the little door , not know whither she be go .
By this time night have fall , and Tephany be very tired .
Thankfully she find herself at the gate of a convent , and ask if she might stay there till morning .
But the portress answer roughly that it be no place for beggar , and bid her begone , so the poor girl drag herself slowly along the road , till a light and the bark of a dog tell her that she be near a farm .
In front of the house be a group of people ; two or three woman and the son of the farmer .
When their mother hear Tephany 's request to be give a bed the good wife 's heart soften , and she be just go to invite her inside , when the young men , whose head be turn by the girl 's beauty , begin to quarrel a to which should do most for her .
From word they come to blow , and the woman , frighten at the disturbance , pelt Tephany with insulting name .
She quickly run down the near path , hop to escape them in the darkness of the tree , but in an instant she hear their footstep behind her .
Wild with fear her leg tremble under her , when suddenly she bethink herself of her necklace .
With a violent effort she burst the clasp and flung it round the neck of a pig which be grunt in a ditch , and a she do so she hear the footstep cease from pursue her and run after the pig , for her charm have vanish .
On she go , scarcely know where she be go , till she find herself , to her surprise and joy , close to her aunt 's house .
For several day she felt so tired and unhappy that she could hardly get through her work , and to make matter bad Denis scarcely ever come near her .
` He be too busy , ' he say , ` and really it be only rich people who could afford to waste time in talk . '
As the day go on Tephany grow paler and paler , till everybody notice it except her aunt .
The water-pot be almost too heavy for her now , but morning and evening she carry it to the spring , though the effort to lift it to her shoulder be often too much for her .
` How could I have be so foolish , ' she whisper to herself , when she go down as usual at sunset .
` It be not freedom to see Denis that I should have ask for , for he be soon weary of me , nor a quick tongue , for he be afraid of it , nor beauty , for that bring me nothing but trouble , but rich which make life easy both for oneself and others .
Ah !
if I only dare to beg this gift from the fairy , I should be wise than before and know how to choose good . '
` Be satisfy , ' say the voice of the old woman , who seem to be stand unseen at Tephany 's elbow .
` If you look in your right-hand pocket when you go home you will find a small box .
Rub your eye with the ointment it contain , and you will see that you yourself contain a priceless treasure . '
Tephany do not in the least understand what she mean , but run back to the farm as fast a she could , and begin to fumble joyfully in her right-hand pocket .
Sure enough , there be the little box with the precious ointment .
She be in the act of rub her eye with it when Barbaik Bourhis enter the room .
Ever since she have be oblige to leave her work and pass her time , she do not know why , in count cabbage , everything have go wrong , and she could not get a labourer to stay with her because of her bad temper .
When , therefore , she saw her niece stand quietly before her mirror , Barbaik break out : ` So this be what you do when I be out in the field !
Ah !
it be no wonder if the farm be ruin .
Are you not ashamed , girl , to behave so ? '
Tephany try to stammer some excuse , but her aunt be half mad with rage , and a box on the ear be her only answer .
At this Tephany , hurt , bewilder and excite , could control herself no longer , and turn away burst into tear .
But what be her surprise when she saw that each tear-drop be a round and shin pearl .
Barbaik , who also behold this marvel , utter a cry of astonishment , and throw herself on her knee to pick them up from the floor .
She be still gather them when the door open and in come Denis .
` Pearls !
Are they really pearl ? '
he ask , fall on his knee also , and look up at Tephany he perceive others still more beautiful roll down the girl 's cheek .
` Take care not to let any of the neighbour hear of it , Denis , ' say Barbaik .
` Of course you shall have your share , but nobody else shall get a single one .
Cry on , my dear , cry on , ' she continue to Tephany .
It be for your good as well a ours , ' and she hold out her apron to catch them , and Denis his hat .
But Tephany could hardly bear any more .
She felt half choke at the sight of their greediness , and want to rush from the hall , and though Barbaik catch her arm to prevent this , and say all sort of tender word which she think would make the girl weep the more , Tephany with a violent effort force back her tear , and wipe her eye .
` Is she finish already ? '
cry Barbaik , in a tone of disappointment .
` Oh , try again , my dear .
Do you think it would do any good to beat her a little ? '
she add to Denis , who shake his head .
` That be enough for the first time .
I will go into the town and find out the value of each pearl . '
` Then I will go with you , ' say Barbaik , who never trust anyone and be afraid of be cheat .
So the two go out , leave Tephany behind them .
She sit quite still on her chair , her hand clasp tightly together , a if she be force something back .
At last she raise her eye , which have be fix on the ground , and behold the fairy standing in a dark corner by the hearth , observe her with a mocking look .
The girl tremble and jump up , then , take the feather , the pin , and the box , she hold them out to the old woman .
` Here they be , all of them , ' she cry ; ` they belong to you .
Let me never see them again , but I have learn the lesson that they teach me .
Others may have rich , beauty and wit , but a for me I desire nothing but to be the poor peasant girl I always be , work hard for those she love . '
` Yes , you have learn your lesson , ' answer the fairy , ` and now you shall lead a peaceful life and marry the man you love .
For after all it be not yourself you think of but him . '
Never again do Tephany see the old woman , but she forgive Denis for sell her tear , and in time he grow to be a good husband , who do his own share of work .
From ` Le Foyer Breton , ' par E. Souvestre .
The Groac ' h of the Isle of Lok In old time , when all kind of wonderful thing happen in Brittany , there live in the village of Lanillis , a young man name Houarn Pogamm and a girl call Bellah Postik .
They be cousin , and a their mother be great friend , and constantly in and out of each other 's house , they have often be lay in the same cradle , and have play and fight over their game .
` When they be grow up they will marry , ' say the mother ; but just a every one be begin to think of wed bell , the two mother die , and the cousin , who have no money , go a servant in the same house .
This be good than be part , of course , but not so good a have a little cottage of their own , where they could do a they like , and soon they might have be hear bewail to each other the hardness of their lot .
` If we could only manage to buy a cow and get a pig to fatten , ' grumble Houarn , ' I would rent a bit of ground from the master , and then we could be marry . '
` Yes , ' answer Bellah , with a deep sigh ; ` but we live in such hard time , and at the last fair the price of pig have rise again . '
` We shall have long to wait , that be quite clear , ' reply Houarn , turn away to his work .
Whenever they meet they repeat their grievance , and at length Houarn 's patience be exhaust , and one morning he come to Bellah and tell her that he be go away to seek his fortune .
The girl be very unhappy a she listen to this , and felt sorry that she have not try to make the best of thing .
She implore Houarn not to leave her , but he would listen to nothing .
` The bird , ' he say , ` continue fly until they reach a field of corn , and the bee do not stop unless they find the honey-giving flower , and why should a man have less sense than they ?
Like them , I shall seek till I get what I want -- that be , money to buy a cow and a pig to fatten .
And if you love me , Bellah , you wo n't attempt to hinder a plan which will hasten our marriage . '
The girl saw it be useless to say more , so she answer sadly : ` Well , go then , since you must .
But first I will divide with you all that my parent leave me , ' and go to her room , she open a small chest , and take from it a bell , a knife , and a little stick .
` This bell , ' she say , ` can be hear at any distance , however far , but it only ring to warn u that our friend be in great danger .
The knife free all it touch from the spell that have be lay on them ; while the stick will carry you wherever you want to go .
I will give you the knife to guard you against the enchantment of wizard , and the bell to tell me of your peril .
The stick I shall keep for myself , so that I can fly to you if ever you have need of me . '
Then they cry for a little on each other 's neck , and Houarn start for the mountain .
But in those day , a in these , beggar abound , and through every village he pass they follow Houarn in crowd , mistake him for a gentleman , because there be no hole in his clothes .
` There be no fortune to be make here , ' he think to himself ; ` it be a place for spending , and not earn .
I see I must go far , ' and he walk on to Pont-aven , a pretty little town build on the bank of a river .
He be sit on a bench outside an inn , when he hear two men who be load their mule talk about the Groac ' h of the island of Lok .
` What be a Groac ` h ? '
ask he . '
I have never come across one . '
And the men answer that it be the name give to the fairy that dwell in the lake , and that she be rich -- oh !
rich than all the king in the world put together .
Many have go to the island to try and get possession of her treasure , but no one have ever come back .
As he listen Houarn 's mind be make up . '
I will go , and return too , ' he say to the muleteer .
They star at him in astonishment , and beseech him not to be so mad and to throw away his life in such a foolish manner ; but he only laugh , and answer that if they could tell him of any other way in which to procure a cow and a pig to fatten , he would think no more about it .
But the men do not know how this be to be do , and , shake their head over his obstinacy , leave him to his fate .
So Houarn go down to the sea , and find a boatman who engage to take him to the isle of Lok .
The island be large , and lie almost across it be a lake , with a narrow opening to the sea .
Houarn pay the boatman and send him away , and then proceed to walk round the lake .
At one end he perceive a small skiff , paint blue and shape like a swan , lie under a clump of yellow broom .
As far a he could see , the swan 's head be tuck under it wing , and Houarn , who have never behold a boat of the sort , go quickly towards it and step in , so a to examine it the good .
But no sooner be he on board than the swan wake suddenly up ; his head emerge from under his wing , his foot begin to move in the water , and in another moment they be in the middle of the lake .
As soon a the young man have recover from his surprise , he prepare to jump into the lake and swim to shore .
But the bird have guess his intention , and plunge beneath the water , carry Houarn with him to the palace of the Groac ` h. Now , unless you have be under the sea and behold all the wonder that lie there , you can never have an idea what the Groac ` h 's palace be like .
It be all make of shell , blue and green and pink and lilac and white , shade into each other till you could not tell where one colour end and the other begin .
The staircase be of crystal , and every separate stair sang like a woodland bird a you put your foot on it .
Round the palace be great garden full of all the plant that grow in the sea , with diamond for flower .
In a large hall the Groac ' h be lie on a couch of gold .
The pink and white of her face remind you of the shell of her palace , while her long black hair be intertwine with string of coral , and her dress of green silk seem form out of the sea .
At the sight of her Houarn stop , dazzle by her beauty .
` Come in , ' say the Groac ` h , rise to her foot .
` Strangers and handsome youth be always welcome here .
Do not be shy , but tell me how you find your way , and what you want . '
` My name be Houarn , ' he answer , ` Lanillis be my home , and I be try to earn enough money to buy a little cow and a pig to fatten . '
` Well , you can easily get that , ' reply she ; ` it be nothing to worry about .
Come in and enjoy yourself . '
And she beckon him to follow her into a second hall whose floor and wall be form of pearl , while down the side there be table laden with fruit and wine of all kind ; and a he eat and drink , the Groac ' h talk to him and tell him how the treasure he saw come from shipwreck vessel , and be bring to her palace by a magic current of water . '
I do not wonder , ' exclaim Houarn , who now felt quite at home -- ' I do not wonder that the people on the earth have so much to say about you . '
` The rich be always envy . '
` For myself , ' he add , with a laugh , ' I only ask for the half of your wealth . '
` You can have it , if you will , Houarn , ' answer the fairy .
` What do you mean ? '
cry he .
` My husband , Korandon , be dead , ' she reply , ` and if you wish it , I will marry you . '
The young man gaze at her in surprise .
Could any one so rich and so beautiful really wish to be his wife ?
He look at her again , and Bellah be forget a he answer : ' A man would be mad indeed to refuse such an offer .
I can only accept it with joy . '
` Then the sooner it be do the good , ' say the Groac ` h , and give order to her servant .
After that be finish , she beg Houarn to accompany her to a fish-pond at the bottom of the garden .
` Come lawyer , come miller , come tailor , come singer ! '
cry she , hold out a net of steel ; and at each summons a fish appear and jump into the net .
When it be full she go into a large kitchen and throw them all into a golden pot ; but above the bubbling of the water Houarn seem to hear the whispering of little voice .
` Who be it whisper in the golden pot , Groac ` h ? '
he inquire at last .
` It be nothing but the noise of the wood sparkling , ' she answer ; but it do not sound the least like that to Houarn .
` There it be again , ' he say , after a short pause .
` The water be get hot , and it make the fish jump , ' she reply ; but soon the noise grow louder and like cry .
` What be it ? '
ask Houarn , begin to feel uncomfortable .
` Just the cricket on the hearth , ' say she , and break into a song which drown the cry from the pot .
But though Houarn hold his peace , he be not as happy a before .
Something seem to have go wrong , and then he suddenly remember Bellah .
` Is it possible I can have forget her so soon ?
What a wretch I be ! '
he think to himself ; and he remain apart and watch the Groac ' h while she empty the fish into a plate , and bid him eat his dinner while she fetch wine from her cellar in a cave .
Houarn sit down and take out the knife which Bellah have give him , but as soon a the blade touch the fish the enchantment cease , and four men stand before him .
` Houarn , save u , we entreat you , and save yourself too ! '
murmur they , not dare to raise their voice .
` Why , it must have be you who be cry out in the pot just now ! '
exclaim Houarn .
` Yes , it be u , ' they answer .
` Like you , we come to the isle of Lok to seek our fortune , and like you we consent to marry the Groac ` h , and no sooner be the ceremony over than she turn u into fish , a she have do to all our forerunner , who be in the fish-pond still , where you will shortly join them . '
On hear this Houarn leap into the air , a if he already felt himself frizzle in the golden pot .
He rush to the door , hop to escape that way ; but the Groac ` h , who have hear everything , meet him on the threshold .
Instantly she throw the steel net over his head , and the eye of a little green frog peep through the mesh .
` You shall go and play with the rest , ' she say , carry him off to the fish-pond .
It be at this very moment that Bellah , who be skim the milk in the farm dairy , hear the fairy bell tinkle violently .
At the sound she grow pale , for she know it mean that Houarn be in danger ; and , hastily , change the rough dress she wear for her work , she leave the farm with the magic stick in her hand .
Her knee be tremble under her , but she run as fast a she could to the cross road , where she drive her stick into the ground , murmur a she do so a verse her mother have teach her : Little staff of apple-tree , Over the earth and over the sea , Up in the air be guide to me , Everywhere to wander free , and immediately the stick become a smart little horse , with a rosette at each ear and a feather on his forehead .
He stand quite still while Bellah scramble up , then he start off , his pace grow quick and quick , till at length the girl could hardly see the tree and house a they flash past .
But , rapid a the pace be , it be not rapid enough for Bellah , who stoop and say : ` The swallow be less swift than the wind , the wind be less swift than the lightning .
But you , my horse , if you love me , must be swift than them all , for there be a part of my heart that suffers -- the best part of my heart that be in danger . '
And the horse hear her , and gallop like a straw carry along by a tempest till they reach the foot of a rock call the Leap of the Deer .
There he stop , for no horse or mule that ever be bear could climb that rock , and Bellah know it , so she begin to sing again : Horse of Leon , give to me , Over the earth and over the sea , Up in the air be guide to me , Everywhere to wander free , and when she have finish , the horse 's fore leg grow short and spread into wing , his hind leg become claws , feather sprout all over his body , and she sit on the back of a great bird , which bore her to the summit of the rock .
Here she find a nest made of clay and line with dried moss , and in the centre a tiny man , black and wrinkled , who give a cry of surprise at the sight of Bellah .
` Ah !
you be the pretty girl who be to come and save me ! '
` To save you ! '
repeat Bellah .
` But who be you , my little friend ? ' '
I be the husband of the Groac ' h of the isle of Lok , and it be owe to her that I be here . '
` But what be you do in this nest ? ' '
I be sit on six egg of stone , and I shall not be set free till they be hatch . '
On hear this Bellah begin to laugh .
` Poor little cock ! '
she say , ` and how be I to deliver you ? '
` By deliver Houarn , who be in the power of the Groac ` h. ' ` Ah !
tell me how I can manage that , and if I have to walk round the whole of Brittany on my bended knee I will do it ! '
` Well , first you must dress yourself a a young man , and then go and seek the Groac ` h .
When you have find her you must contrive to get hold of the net of steel that hang from her waist , and shut her up in it for ever . '
` But where be I to find a young man 's clothes ? '
ask she . '
I will show you , ' he reply , and a he speak he pull out three of his red hair and blow them away , mutter something the while .
In the twinkling of an eye the four hair change into four tailor , of whom the first carry a cabbage , the second a pair of scissors , the third a needle , and the fourth an iron .
Without wait for order , they sit down in the nest and , cross their leg comfortably , begin to prepare the suit of clothes for Bellah .
With one of the leaf of the cabbage they make her a coat , and another serve for a waistcoat ; but it take two for the wide breech which be then in fashion .
The hat be cut from the heart of the cabbage , and a pair of shoe from the thick stem .
And when Bellah have put them all on you would have take her for a gentleman dress in green velvet , line with white satin .
She thank the little men gratefully , and after a few more instruction , jump on the back of her great bird , and be bear away to the isle of Lok .
Once there , she bid him transform himself back into a stick , and with it in her hand she step into the blue boat , which conduct her to the palace of shell .
The Groac ' h seem overjoyed to see her , and tell her that never before have she behold such a handsome young man .
Very soon she lead her visitor into the great hall , where wine and fruit be always wait , and on the table lay the magic knife , leave there by Houarn .
Unseen by the Groac ` h , Bellah hide it in a pocket of her green coat , and then follow her hostess into the garden , and to the pond which contain the fish , their side shin with a thousand different colour .
` Oh !
what beautiful , beautiful creature ! '
say she .
` I 'm sure I should never be tire of watch them . '
And she sit down on the bank , with her elbow on her knee and her chin in her hand , her eye fix on the fish a they flash past .
` Would you not like to stay here always ? '
ask the Groac ` h ; and Bellah answer that she desire nothing well .
` Then you have only to marry me , ' say the Groac ` h. ` Oh !
do n't say no , for I have fall deeply in love with you . '
` Well , I wo n't say `` No , '' ' reply Bellah , with a laugh , ` but you must promise first to let me catch one of those lovely fish in your net . '
` It be not so easy a it look , ' rejoin the Groac ` h , smile , ` but take it , and try your luck . '
Bellah take the net which the Groac ' h hold out , and , turn rapidly , fling it over the witch 's head .
` Become in body what you be in soul ! '
cry she , and in an instant the lovely fairy of the sea be a toad , horrible to look upon .
She struggle hard to tear the net asunder , but it be no use .
Bellah only draw it the tighter , and , fling the sorceress into a pit , she roll a great stone across the mouth , and leave her .
As she draw near the pond she saw a great procession of fish advance to meet her , cry in hoarse tone : ` This be our lord and master , who have save u from the net of steel and the pot of gold ! '
` And who will restore you to your proper shape , ' say Bellah , draw the knife from her pocket .
But just a she be go to touch the foremost fish , her eye fell on a green frog on his knee beside her , his little paw cross over his little heart .
Bellah felt a if finger be tighten round her throat , but she manage to cry : ` Is this you , my Houarn ?
Is this you ? '
` It be I , ' croak the little frog ; and a the knife touch him he be a man again , and , spring up , he clasp her in his arm .
` But we must not forget the others , ' she say at last , and begin to transform the fish to their proper shape .
There be so many of them that it take quite a long time .
Just a she have finish there arrive the little dwarf from the Deer 's Leap in a car drawn by six cockchafer , which once have be the six stone egg .
` Here I be ! '
he exclaim .
` You have break the spell that hold me , and now come and get your reward , ' and , dismount from his chariot , he lead them down into the cave fill with gold and jewel , and bid Bellah and Houarn take as much a they want .
When their pocket be full , Bellah order her stick to become a winged carriage , large enough to bear them and the men they have rescue back to Lanillis .
There they be marry the next day , but instead of set up housekeep with the little cow and pig to fatten that they have so long wished for , they be able to buy land for mile round for themselves , and give each man who have be deliver from the Groac ' h a small farm , where he live happily to the end of his day .
From ` Le Foyer Breton , ' par E. Souvestre .
The Escape of the Mouse Manawyddan the prince and his friend Pryderi be wanderer , for the brother of Manawyddan have be slay , and his throne take from him .
Very sorrowful be Manawyddan , but Pryderi be stout of heart , and bid him be of good cheer , a he know a way out of his trouble .
` And what may that be ? '
ask Manawyddan .
` It be that thou marry my mother Rhiannon and become lord of the fair land that I will give her for dowry .
Never do any lady have more wit than she , and in her youth none be more lovely ; even yet she be good to look upon . '
` Thou art the best friend that ever a man have , ' say Manawyddan .
` Let u go now to seek Rhiannon , and the land where she dwell . '
Then they set forth , but the news of their come ran swifter still , and Rhiannon and Kieva , wife of Pryderi , make haste to prepare a feast for them .
And Manawyddan find that Pryderi have speak the truth concern his mother , and ask if she would take him for her husband .
Right gladly do she consent , and without delay they be marry , and ride away to the hunt , Rhiannon and Manawyddan , Kieva and Pryderi , and they would not be part from each other by night or by day , so great be the love between them .
One day , when they be return , they be sit out in a green place , and suddenly the crash of thunder strike loudly on their ear , and a wall of mist fell between them , so that they be hide one from the other .
