The princess be know to love beautiful thing , perhaps she might like to buy some ? '
Now the princess have be wonder for many day what trim she should put on her dress , so that they should outshine the dress of the other lady at the court ball .
Nothing that she think of seemed good enough , so , when the message be bring that the ogre and his ware be below , she at once order that he should be bring to her chamber .
Oh !
what beautiful stone he lay before her ; what lovely ruby , and what rare pearl !
No other lady would have jewel like those -- of that the princess be quite sure ; but she cast down her eye so that the ogre might not see how much she long for them . '
I fear they be too costly for me , ' she say carelessly ; ` and besides , I have hardly need of any more jewel just now . ' '
I have no particular wish to sell them myself , ' answer the ogre , with equal indifference .
` But I have a necklace of shin stone which be leave me by father , and one , the large engraven with weird character , be miss .
I have hear that it be in your husband 's possession , and if you can get me that stone you shall have any of these jewel that you choose .
But you will have to pretend that you want it for yourself ; and , above all , do not mention me , for he set great store by it , and would never part with it to a stranger !
To-morrow I will return with some jewel yet fine than those I have with me to-day .
So , madam , farewell ! '
Left alone , the princess begin to think of many thing , but chiefly a to whether she would persuade her husband to give her the stone or not .
At one moment she felt he have already bestow so much upon her that it be a shame to ask for the only object he have keep back .
No , it would be mean ; she could not do it !
But then , those diamond , and those string of pearl !
After all , they have only be marry a week , and the pleasure of give it to her ought to be far great than the pleasure of keep it for himself .
And she be sure it would be !
Well , that evening , when the young man have sup off his favourite dish which the princess take care to have specially prepare for him , she sit down close beside him , and begin stroke his head .
For some time she do not speak , but listen attentively to all the adventure that have befall him that day .
` But I be think of you all the time , ' say he at the end , ` and wish that I could bring you back something you would like .
But , ala !
what be there that you do not possess already ? '
` How good of you not to forget me when you be in the midst of such danger and hardship , ' answer she .
` Yes , it be true I have many beautiful thing ; but if you want to give me a present -- and to-morrow be my birthday -- there IS one thing that I wish for very much . '
` And what be that ?
Of course you shall have it directly ! '
he ask eagerly .
` It be that bright stone which fell out of the fold of your turban a few day ago , ' she answer , play with his finger ; ` the little stone with all those funny mark upon it .
I never saw any stone like it before . '
The young man do not answer at first ; then he say , slowly : ' I have promise , and therefore I must perform .
But will you swear never to part from it , and to keep it safely about you always ?
More I can not tell you , but I beg you earnestly to take heed to this . '
The princess be a little startle by his manner , and begin to be sorry that she have every listen to the ogre .
But she do not like to draw back , and pretend to be immensely delighted at her new toy , and kiss and thank her husband for it .
` After all I need n't give it to the ogre , ' think she a she drop off to sleep .
Unluckily the next morning the young man go hunt again , and the ogre , who be watch , know this , and do not come till much later than before .
At the moment that he knock at the door of the palace the princess have tire of all her employment , and her attendant be at their wit ' end how to amuse her , when a tall negro dress in scarlet come to announce that the ogre be below , and desire to know if the princess would speak to him .
` Bring him hither at once ! '
cry she , spring up from her cushion , and forget all her resolve of the previous night .
In another moment she be bend with rapture over the glittering gem .
` Have you get it ? '
ask the ogre in a whisper , for the princess 's lady be stand as near a they dare to catch a glimpse of the beautiful jewel .
` Yes , here , ' she answer , slip the stone from her sash and place it among the rest .
Then she raise her voice , and begin to talk quickly of the price of the chain and necklace , and after some bargaining , to deceive the attendant , she declare that she like one string of pearl good than all the rest , and that the ogre might take away the other thing , which be not half as valuable a he suppose .
` As you please , madam , ' say he , bow himself out of the palace .
Soon after he have go a curious thing happen .
The princess carelessly touch the wall of her room , which be wont to reflect the warm red light of the fire on the hearth , and find her hand quite wet .
She turn round , and -- be it her fancy ?
or do the fire burn more dimly than before ?
Hurriedly she pass into the picture gallery , where pool of water show here and there on the floor , and a cold chill run through her whole body .
At that instant her frightened lady come run down the stair , cry : ` Madam !
madam !
what have happen ?
The palace be disappear under our eye ! '
` My husband will be home very soon , ' answer the princess -- who , though nearly as much frighten a her lady , felt that she must set them a good example .
` Wait till then , and he will tell u what to do . '
So they wait , seat on the high chair they could find , wrap in their warm garment , and with pile of cushion under their foot , while the poor bird fly with numbed wing hither and thither , till they be so lucky a to discover an open window in some forgotten corner .
Through this they vanish , and be see no more .
At last , when the princess and her lady have be force to leave the upper room , where the wall and floor have melt away , and to take refuge in the hall , the young man come home .
He have ride back along a wind road from which he do not see the palace till he be close upon it , and stand horrify at the spectacle before him .
He know in an instant that his wife must have betray his trust , but he would not reproach her , a she must be suffer enough already .
Hurrying on he spring over all that be leave of the palace wall , and the princess give a cry of relief at the sight of him .
` Come quickly , ' he say , ` or you will be frozen to death ! '
And a dreary little procession set out for the king 's palace , the greyhound and the cat bring up the rear .
At the gate he leave them , though his wife beseech him to allow her to enter .
` You have betray me and ruin me , ' he say sternly ; ' I go to seek my fortune alone . '
And without another word he turn and leave her .
With his falcon on his wrist , and his greyhound and cat behind him , the young man walk a long way , inquire of everyone he meet whether they have see his enemy the ogre .
But nobody have .
Then he bid his falcon fly up into the sky -- up , up , and up -- and try if his sharp eye could discover the old thief .
The bird have to go so high that he do not return for some hour ; but he tell his master that the ogre be lie asleep in a splendid palace in a far country on the shore of the sea .
This be delightful news to the young man , who instantly buy some meat for the falcon , bid him make a good meal .
` To-morrow , ' say he , ` you will fly to the palace where the ogre lie , and while he be asleep you will search all about him for a stone on which be engrave strange sign ; this you will bring to me .
In three day I shall expect you back here . '
` Well , I must take the cat with me , ' answer the bird .
The sun have not yet rise before the falcon soar high into the air , the cat seat on his back , with his paw tightly clasp the bird 's neck .
` You have good shut your eye or you may get giddy , ' say the bird ; and the cat , you have never before be off the ground except to climb a tree , do a she be bid .
All that day and all that night they fly , and in the morning they saw the ogre 's palace lie beneath them .
` Dear me , ' say the cat , open her eye for the first time , ` that look to me very like a rat city down there , let u go down to it ; they may be able to help u . '
So they alight in some bush in the heart of the rat city .
The falcon remain where he be , but the cat lay down outside the principal gate , cause terrible excitement among the rat .
At length , see she do not move , one bolder than the rest put it head out of an upper window of the castle , and say , in a trembling voice : ` Why have you come here ?
What do you want ?
If it be anything in our power , tell u , and we will do it . '
` If you would have let me speak to you before , I would have tell you that I come a a friend , ' reply the cat ; ` and I shall be greatly oblige if you would send four of the strong and cunningest among you , to do me a service . '
` Oh , we shall be delight , ' answer the rat , much relieve .
` But if you will inform me what it be you wish them to do I shall be well able to judge who be most fitted for the post . ' '
I thank you , ' say the cat .
` Well , what they have to do be this : To-night they must burrow under the wall of the castle and go up to the room be an ogre lie asleep .
Somewhere about him he have hide a stone , on which be engrave strange sign .
When they have find it they must take it from him without his waking , and bring it to me . '
` Your order shall be obey , ' reply the rat .
And he go out to give his instruction .
About midnight the cat , who be still sleep before the gate , be awaken by some water flung at her by the head rat , who could not make up his mind to open the door .
` Here be the stone you want , ' say he , when the cat start up with a loud mew ; ` if you will hold up your paw I will drop it down . '
And so he do .
` And now farewell , ' continue the rat ; ` you have a long way to go , and will do well to start before daybreak . '
` Your counsel be good , ' reply the cat , smile to itself ; and put the stone in her mouth she go off to seek the falcon .
Now all this time neither the cat nor the falcon have have any food , and the falcon soon get tired carrying such a heavy burden .
When night arrive he declare he could go no far , but would spend it on the bank of a river .
` And it be my turn to take care of the stone , ' say he , ` or it will seem a if you have do everything and I nothing . '
` No , I get it , and I will keep it , ' answer the cat , who be tire and cross ; and they begin a fine quarrel .
But , unluckily , in the midst of it , the cat raise her voice , and the stone fell into the ear of a big fish which happen to be swim by , and though both the cat and the falcon sprang into the water after it , they be too late .
Half drown , and more than half choke , the two faithful servant scramble back to land again .
The falcon fly to a tree and spread his wing in the sun to dry , but the cat , after give herself a good shake , begin to scratch up the sandy bank and to throw the bit into the stream .
` What be you do that for ? '
ask a little fish .
` Do you know that you be make the water quite muddy ? '
` That do n't matter at all to me , ' answer the cat . '
I be go to fill up all the river , so that the fish may die . '
` That be very unkind , a we have never do you any harm , ' reply the fish .
` Why be you so angry with u ? '
` Because one of you have get a stone of mine -- a stone with strange sign upon it -- which drop into the water .
If you will promise to get it back for me , why , perhaps I will leave your river alone . ' '
I will certainly try , ' answer the fish in a great hurry ; ` but you must have a little patience , a it may not be an easy task . '
And in an instant his scale might be see flash quickly along .
The fish swam as fast a he could to the sea , which be not far distant , and call together all his relation who live in the neighbourhood , he tell them of the terrible danger which threaten the dweller in the river .
` None of u have get it , ' say the fish , shake their head ; ` but in the bay yonder there be a tunny who , although he be so old , always go everywhere .
He will be able to tell you about it , if anyone can . '
So the little fish swam off to the tunny , and again related his story .
` Why I be up that river only a few hour ago ! '
cry the tunny ; ` and a I be come back something fell into my ear , and there it be still , for I go to sleep , when I get home and forget all about it .
Perhaps it may be what you want . '
And stretch up his tail he whisk out the stone .
` Yes , I think that must be it , ' say the fish with joy .
And take the stone in his mouth he carry it to the place where the cat be wait for him . '
I be much oblige to you , ' say the cat , a the fish lay the stone on the sand , ` and to reward you , I will let your river alone . '
And she mount the falcon 's back , and they fly to their master .
Ah , how glad he be to see them again with the magic stone in their possession .
In a moment he have wish for a palace , but this time it be of green marble ; and then he wish for the princess and her lady to occupy it .
And there they live for many year , and when the old king die the princess 's husband reign in his stead .
The Story of Manus -LSB- Adapted from Contes Berberes . -RSB-
Far away over the sea of the West there reign a king who have two son ; and the name of the one be Oireal , and the name of the other be Iarlaid .
When the boy be still child , their father and mother die , and a great council be hold , and a man be choose from among them who would rule the kingdom till the boy be old enough to rule it themselves .
The year pass on , and by-and-by another council be hold , and it be agree that the king 's son be now of an age to take the power which rightly belong to them .
So the youth be bidden to appear before the council , and Oireal the elder be small and weak than his brother . '
I like not to leave the deer on the hill and the fish in the river , and sit in judgment on my people , ' say Oireal , when he have listen to the word of the chief of the council .
And the chief waxed angry , and answer quickly : ` Not one clod of earth shall ever be yours if this day you do not take on yourself the vow that be take by the king your father . '
Then spake Iarlaid , the young , and he say : ` Let one half be yours , and the other give to me ; then you will have few people to rule over . '
` Yes , I will do that , ' answered Oireal .
After this , one half of the men of the land of Lochlann do homage to Oireal , and the other half to Iarlaid .
And they govern their kingdom a they would , and in a few year they become grown men with beard on their chin ; and Iarlaid marry the daughter of the king of Greece , and Oireal the daughter of the king of Orkney .
The next year son be bear to Oireal and Iarlaid ; and the son of Oireal be big and strong , but the son of Iarlaid be little and weak , and each have six foster brother who go everywhere with the prince .
One day Manus , son of Oireal , and his cousin , the son of Iarlaid , call to their foster brother , and bid them come and play a game at shinny in the great field near the school where they be teach all that prince and noble should know .
Long they play , and swiftly do the ball pas from one to another , when Manus drive the ball at his cousin , the son of Iarlaid .
The boy , who be not use to be roughly handle , even in jest , cry out that he be sorely hurt , and go home with his foster brother and tell his tale to his mother .
The wife of Iarlaid grow white and angry a she listen , and thrust her son aside , seek the council hall where Iarlaid be sit .
` Manus have drive a ball at my son , and fain would have slain him , ' say she .
` Let an end be put to him and his ill deed . '
But Iarlaid answer : ` Nay , I will not slay the son of my brother . '
` And he shall not slay my son , ' say the queen .
And call to her chamberlain she order him to lead the prince to the four brown boundary of the world , and to leave him there with a wise man , who would care for him , and let no harm befall him .
And the wise man set the boy on the top of a hill where the sun always shone , and he could see every man , but no man could see him .
Then she summon Manus to the castle , and for a whole year she keep him fast , and his own mother could not get speech of him .
But in the end , when the wife of Oireal fell sick , Manus flee from the tower which be his prison , and steal back to his on home .
For a few year he stay there in peace , and then the wife of Iarlaid his uncle send for him .
` It be time that you be marry , ' she say , when she saw that Manus have grow tall and strong like unto Iarlaid .
` Tall and strong you be , and comely of face .
I know a bride that will suit you well , and that be the daughter of the mighty earl of Finghaidh , that do homage for his land to me .
I myself will go with a great following to his house , and you shall go with me . '
Thus it be do ; and though the earl 's wife be eager to keep her daughter with her yet a while , she be fain to yield , a the wife of Iarlaid vow that not a rood of land should the earl have , unless he do her bidding .
But if he would give his daughter to Manus , she would bestow on him the third part of her own kingdom , with much treasure beside .
This she do , not from love to Manus , but because she wish to destroy him .
So they be marry , and ride back with the wife of Iarlaid to her own palace .
And that night , while he be sleep , there come a wise man , who be his father 's friend , and awake him say : ` Danger lie very close to you , Manus , son of Oireal .
You hold yourself favour because you have a a bride the daughter of a mighty earl ; but do you know what bride the wife of Iarlaid sought for her own son ?
It be no worldly wife she find for him , but the swift March wind , and never can you prevail against her . '
` Is it thus ? '
answer Manu .
And at the first streak of dawn he go to the chamber where the queen lay in the midst of her maiden . '
I have come , ' he say , ` for the third part of the kingdom , and for the treasure which you promise me . '
But the wife of Iarlaid laugh a she hear him .
` Not a clod shall you have here , ' spake she .
` You must go to the Old Bergen for that .
Mayhap under it stone and rough mountain you may find a treasure ! '
` Then give me your son 's six foster brother as well a my own , ' answer he .
And the queen give them to him , and they set out for Old Bergen .
A year pass by , and find them still in that wild land , hunt the reindeer , and dig pit for the mountain sheep to fall into .
For a time Manus and his companion live merrily , but at length Manus grow weary of the strange country , and they all take ship for the land of Lochlann .
The wind be fierce and cold , and long be the voyage ; but , one spring day , they sail into the harbour that lay beneath the castle of Iarlaid .
The queen look from her window and behold him mount the hill , with the twelve foster brother behind him .
Then she say to her husband : ` Manus have return with his twelve foster brother .
Would that I could put an end to him and his murdering and his slaying . '
` That be a great pity , ' answer Iarlaid .
` And it be not I that will do it . '
` If you will not do it I will , ' say she .
And she call the twelve foster brother and make them vow fealty to herself .
So Manus be leave with no man , and sorrowful be he when he return alone to Old Bergen .
It be late when his foot touch the shore , and take the path towards the forest .
On his way there meet him a man in a red tunic .
` Is it you , Manus , come back again ? '
ask he .
` It be I , ' answered Manus ; ` alone have I return from the land of Lochlann . '
The man eye him silently for a moment , and then he say : ' I dream that you be gird with a sword and become king of Lochlann . '
But Manus answer : ' I have no sword and my bow be break . ' '
I will give you a new sword if you will make me a promise , ' say the man once more .
` To be sure I will make it , if ever I be king , ' answer Manus .
` But speak , and tell me what promise I be to make . ' '
I be your grandfather 's armourer , ' reply the man , ` and I wish to be your armourer also . '
` That I will promise readily , ' say Manus ; and follow the man into his house , which be at a little distance .
But the house be not like other house , for the wall of every room be hang so thick with arm that you could not see the board .
` Choose what you will , ' say the man ; and Manus unhook a sword and try it across his knee , and it break , and so do the next , and the next .
` Leave off break the sword , ' cry the man , ` and look at this old sword and helmet and tunic that I wear in the war of your grandfather .
Perhaps you may find them of stouter steel . '
And Manus bend the sword thrice across his knee but he could not break it .
So he gird it to his side , and put on the old helmet .
As he fasten the strap his eye fell on a cloth flap outside the window .
` What cloth be that ? '
ask he .
` It be a cloth that be weave by the Little People of the forest , ' say the man ; ` and when you be hungry it will give you food and drink , and if you meet a foe , he will not hurt you , but will stoop and kiss the back of your hand in token of submission .
Take it , and use it well . '
Manus gladly wrap the shawl round his arm , and be leave the house , when he hear the rattling of a chain blow by the wind .
` What chain be that ? '
ask he .
` The creature who have that chain round his neck , need not fear a hundred enemy , ' answer the armourer .
And Manus wind it round him and pass on into the forest .
Suddenly there spring out from the bush two lion , and a lion cub with them .
The fierce beast bound towards him , roar loudly , and would fain have eat him , but quickly Manus stoop and spread the cloth upon the ground .
At that the lion stop , and bow their great head , kiss the back of his wrist and go their way .
But the cub roll itself up in the cloth ; so Manus pick them both up , and carry them with him to Old Bergen .
Another year go by , and then he take the lion cub and set forth to the land of Lochlann .
And the wife of Iarlaid come to meet him , and a brown dog , small but full of courage , come with her .
When the dog behold the lion cub he rush towards him , think to eat him ; but the cub catch the dog by the neck , and shake him , and he be dead .
And the wife of Iarlaid mourn him sore , and her wrath be kindle , and many time she try to slay Manus and his cub , but she could not .
And at last they two go back to Old Bergen , and the twelve foster brother go also .
` Let them go , ' say the wife of Iarlaid , when she hear of it .
` My brother the Red Gruagach will take the head off Manus as well in Old Bergen a elsewhere . '
Now these word be carry by a messenger to the wife of Oireal , and she make haste and send a ship to Old Bergen to bear away her son before the Red Gruagach should take the head off him .
And in the ship be a pilot .
But the wife of Iarlaid make a thick fog to cover the face of the sea , and the rower could not row , l they should drive the ship on to a rock .
And when night come , the lion cub , whose eye be bright and keen , steal up to Manus , and Manus get on his back , and the lion cub sprang ashore and bid Manus rest on the rock and wait for him .
So Manus slept , and by-and-by a voice sound in his ear , say : ` Arise ! '
And he saw a ship in the water beneath him , and in the ship sit the lion cup in the shape of the pilot .
Then they sail away through the fog , and none saw them ; and they reach the land of Lochlann , and the lion cub with the chain round his neck sprang from the ship and Manus follow after .
And the lion cub kill all the men that guard the castle , and Iarlaid and his wife also , so that , in the end , Manus son of Oireal be crown king of Lochlann .
Pinkel the Thief -LSB- Shortened from West Highland Tales . -RSB-
Long , long ago there live a widow who have three son .
The two eldest be grow up , and though they be know to be idle fellow , some of the neighbour have give them work to do on account of the respect in which their mother be hold .
But at the time this story begin they have both be so careless and idle that their master declare they would keep them no longer .
So home they go to their mother and young brother , of whom they think little , because he make himself useful about the house , and look after the hen , and milk the cow .
` Pinkel , ' they call him in scorn , and by-and-by ` Pinkel ' become his name throughout the village .
The two young men think it be much nicer to live at home and be idle than to be oblige to do a quantity of disagreeable thing they do not like , and they would have stay by the fire till the end of their life have not the widow lose patience with them and say that since they would not look for work at home they must seek it elsewhere , for she would not have them under her roof any long .
But she repent bitterly of her word when Pinkel tell her that he too be old enough to go out into the world , and that when he have make a fortune he would send for his mother to keep house for him .
The widow weep many tear at part from her young son , but a she saw that his heart be set upon go with his brother , she do not try to keep him .
So the young men start off one morning in high spirit , never doubt that work such a they might be willing to do would be have for the asking , as soon a their little store of money be spend .
But a very few day of wander open their eye .
Nobody seem to want them , or , if they do , the young men declare that they be not able to undertake all that the farmer or miller or woodcutter require of them .
The young brother , who be wiser , would gladly have do some of the work that the others refuse , but he be small and slight , and no one thought of offer him any .
Therefore they go from one place to another , live only on the fruit and nut they could find in the wood , and get hungry every day .
One night , after they have be walk for many hour and be very tire , they come to a large lake with an island in the middle of it .
From the island stream a strong light , by which they could see everything almost as clearly a if the sun have be shin , and they perceive that , lie half hidden in the rush , be a boat .
` Let u take it and row over to the island , where there must be a house , ' say the eldest brother ; ` and perhaps they will give u food and shelter . '
And they all get in and row across in the direction of the light .
As they draw near the island they saw that it come from a golden lantern hanging over the door of a hut , while sweet tinkle music proceed from some bell attach to the golden horn of a goat which be feed near the cottage .
The young men 's heart rejoice a they think that at last they would be able to rest their weary limb , and they enter the hut , but be amaze to see an ugly old woman inside , wrap in a cloak of gold which light up the whole house .
They look at each other uneasily a she come forward with her daughter , a they know by the cloak that this be a famous witch .
` What do you want ? '
ask she , at the same time signing to her daughter to stir the large pot on the fire .
` We be tired and hungry , and would fain have shelter for the night , ' answer the eldest brother .
` You can not get it here , ' say the witch , ` but you will find both food and shelter in the palace on the other side of the lake .
Take your boat and go ; but leave this boy with me -- I can find work for him , though something tell me he be quick and cunning , and will do me ill . '
` What harm can a poor boy like me do a great Troll like you ? '
answer Pinkel .
` Let me go , I pray you , with my brother .
I will promise never to hurt you . '
And at last the witch let him go , and he follow his brother to the boat .
The way be far than they think , and it be morning before they reach the palace .
Now , at last , their luck seem to have turn , for while the two eldest be give place in the king 's stable , Pinkel be take as page to the little prince .
He be a clever and amuse boy , who saw everything that pass under his eye , and the king notice this , and often employ him in his own service , which make his brother very jealous .
Things go on this way for some time , and Pinkel every day rise in the royal favour .
At length the envy of his brother become so great that they could bear it no longer , and consult together how best they might ruin his credit with the king .
They do not wish to kill him -- though , perhaps , they would not have be sorry if they have heard he be dead -- but merely wish to remind him that he be after all only a child , not half so old and wise a they .
Their opportunity soon come .
It happen to be the king 's custom to visit his stable once a week , so that he might see that his horse be be properly care for .
The next time he enter the stable the two brother manage to be in the way , and when the king praise the beautiful satin skin of the horse under their charge , and remark how different be their condition when his groom have first come across the lake , the young men at once begin to speak of the wonderful light which sprang from the lantern over the hut .
The king , who have a passion for collection all the rare thing he could find , fell into the trap directly , and inquire where he could get this marvellous lantern .
` Send Pinkel for it , Sire , ' say they .
` It belong to an old witch , who no doubt come by it in some evil way .
But Pinkel have a smooth tongue , and he can get the good of any woman , old or young . '
` Then bid him go this very night , ' cry the king ; ` and if he bring me the lantern I will make him one of the chief men about my person . '
Pinkel be much please at the thought of his adventure , and without more ado he borrow a little boat which lay moor to the shore , and row over to the island at once .
It be late by the time he arrive , and almost dark , but he know by the savoury smell that reach him that the witch be cook her supper .
So he climb softly on to the roof , and , peer , watch till the old woman 's back be turn , when he quickly draw a handful of salt from his pocket and throw it into the pot .
Scarcely have he do this when the witch call her daughter and bid her lift the pot off the fire and put the stew into a dish , a it have be cook quite long enough and she be hungry .
But no sooner have she taste it than she put her spoon down , and declare that her daughter must have be meddle with it , for it be impossible to eat anything that be all make of salt .
` Go down to the spring in the valley , and get some fresh water , that I may prepare a fresh supper , ' cry she , ` for I feel half-starved . '
` But , mother , ' answer the girl , ` how can I find the well in this darkness ?
For you know that the lantern 's ray shed no light down there . '
` Well , then , take the lantern with you , ' answer the witch , ` for supper I must have , and there be no water that be nearer . '
So the girl take her pail in one hand and the golden lantern in the other , and hasten away to the well , follow by Pinkel , who take care to keep out of the way of the ray .
When at last she stoop to fill her pail at the well Pinkel push her into it , and snatch up the lantern hurry back to his boat and row off from the shore .
He be already a long distance from the island when the witch , who wonder what have become of her daughter , go to the door to look for her .
Close around the hut be thick darkness , but what be that bob light that stream across the water ?

say she .

take care !

The sun have not yet rise when Pinkel return to the palace , and , enter the king 's chamber , he hold up the lantern so that it ray might fall upon the bed .

At length they remember the goat with golden horn and the bell , and they rejoice ; ` For , ' say they , ` THIS time the old woman will be on the watch , and let him be as clever a he like , the bell on the horn be sure to warn her . '
So when , a before , the king come down to the stable and praise the cleverness of their brother , the young men tell him of that other marvel possess by the witch , the goat with the golden horn .

ask she .
` Yes , dear mother , I have , ' answer Pinkel .

` Yes , dear mother , I be , ' he reply .
And the old witch shout in a rage : ` Ah !
beware how you come hither again , for next time you shall not escape me ! '

The king be so delighted with the goat that he always keep it by his side , night and day ; and , a he have promise , Pinkel be make ruler over the third part of the kingdom .

what be that ? '

So Pinkel be send for , and with a glad heart he set out .
He pass many hour invent first one plan and then another , till he have a scheme ready which he think might prove successful .

ask the witch when she saw him , her eye gleam savagely .

cry she .

And she take down a large knife and begin to sharpen it . '
` Oh !
dear mother , spare me ! '
shriek Pinkel , fall on his knee , and look wildly about him .
` Spare you , indeed , you thief !
Where be my lantern and my goat ?
No !
not !
there be only one fate for robber ! '
And she brandish the knife in the air so that it glitter in the firelight .

I be very hungry , for I have have nothing to eat all day .
Put some poison , if you like , into the porridge , but at least let me have a good meal before I die . '
` That be not a bad idea , ' answer the woman ; ` as long a you do die , it be all one to me . '

` Poisoned or not , the porridge be excellent .

And rub in the poisonous herb , she pour him out half of what remain , and then go to the window to call her cat .

People say that it be the bride who ought to have wear the cloak at her wedding feast ; but the king be so pleased with it that he would not part from it ; and to the end of his life be never see without it .
After his death , Pinkel become king ; and let up hope that he give up his bad and thievish way , and rule his subject well .
As for his brother , he do not punish them , but leave them in the stable , where they grumble all day long .
The Adventures of a Jackal -LSB- Thorpe 's Yule-Tide Stories . -RSB-
In a country which be full of wild beast of all sort there once live a jackal and a hedgehog , and , unlike though they be , the two animal make great friend , and be often see in each other 's company .
One afternoon they be walk along a road together , when the jackal , who be the taller of the two , exclaim : ` Oh !
there be a barn full of corn ; let u go and eat some . '
` Yes , do let u ! '
answer the hedgehog .
So they go to the barn , and eat till they could eat no more .
Then the jackal put on his shoe , which he have take off so a to make no noise , and they return to the high road .
After they have go some way they meet a panther , who stop , and bow politely , say : ` Excuse my speaking to you , but I can not help admire those shoe of yours .
Do you mind tell me who make them ? '
` Yes , I think they be rather nice , ' answer the jackal ; ' I make them myself , though . '
` Could you make me a pair like them ? '
ask the panther eagerly . '
I would do my best , of course , ' reply the jackal ; ` but you must kill me a cow , and when we have eat the flesh I will take the skin and make your shoe out of it . '
So the panther prowl about until he saw a fine cow graze apart from the rest of the herd .
He kill it instantly , and then give a cry to the jackal and hedgehog to come to the place where he be .
They soon skin the dead beast , and spread it skin out to dry , after which they have a grand feast before they curl themselves up for the night , and sleep soundly .
Next morning the jackal get up early and set to work upon the shoe , while the panther sit by and look on with delight .
At last they be finish , and the jackal arose and stretch himself .
` Now go and lay them in the sun out there , ' say he ; ` in a couple of hour they will be ready to put on ; but do not attempt to wear them before , or you will feel them most uncomfortable .
But I see the sun be high in the heaven , and we must be continue our journey . '
The panther , who always believe what everybody tell him , do exactly a he be bid , and in two hour ' time begin to fasten on the shoe .
They certainly set off his paw wonderfully , and he stretch out his forepaw and look at them with pride .
But when he try to walk -- ah !
that be another story !
They be so stiff and hard that he nearly shriek every step he take , and at last he sink down where he be , and actually begin to cry .
After some time some little partridge who be hop about heard the poor panther 's groan , and go up to see what be the matter .
He have never try to make his dinner off them , and they have always be quite friendly .
` You seem in pain , ' say one of them , flutter close to him , ` can we help you ? '
` Oh , it be the jackal !
He make me these shoe ; they be so hard and tight that they hurt my foot , and I can not manage to kick them off . '
` Lie still , and we will soften them , ' answer the kind little partridge .
And call to his brother , they all fly to the near spring , and carry water in their beak , which they pour over the shoe .
This they do till the hard leather grow soft , and the panther be able to slip his foot out of them .
` Oh , thank you , thank you , ' he cry , skip round with joy . '
I feel a different creature .
Now I will go after the jackal and pay him my debt . '
And he bound away into the forest .
But the jackal have be very cunning , and have trot backwards and forward and in and out , so that it be very difficult to know which track he have really follow .
At length , however , the panther catch sight of his enemy , at the same moment that the jackal have catch sight of him .
The panther give a loud roar , and sprang forward , but the jackal be too quick for him and plunge into a dense thicket , where the panther could not follow .
Disgusted with his failure , but more angry than ever , the panther lay down for a while to consider what he should do next , and a he be think , an old man come by .
` Oh !
father , tell me how I can repay the jackal for the way he have serve me ! '
And without more ado he tell his story .
` If you take my advice , ' answer the old man , ` you will kill a cow , and invite all the jackal in the forest to the feast .
Watch them carefully while they be eat , and you will see that most of them keep their eye on their food .
But if one of them glance at you , you will know that be the traitor . '
The panther , whose manner be always good , thank the old man , and follow his counsel .
The cow be kill , and the partridge fly about with invitation to the jackal , who gather in large number to the feast .
The wicked jackal come amongst them ; but a the panther have only see him once he could not distinguish him from the rest .
However , they all take their place on wooden seat place round the dead cow , which be lay across the bough of a fall tree , and begin their dinner , each jackal fix his eye greedily on the piece of meat before him .
Only one of them seem uneasy , and every now and then glance in the direction of his host .
This the panther notice , and suddenly make a bound at the culprit and seize his tail ; but again the jackal be too quick for him , and catch up a knife he cut off his tail and dart into the forest , follow by all the rest of the party .
And before the panther have recover from his surprise he find himself alone .
` What be I to do now ? '
he ask the old man , who soon come back to see how thing have turn out .
` It be very unfortunate , certainly , ' answer he ; ` but I think I know where you can find him .
There be a melon garden about two mile from here , and a jackal be very fond of melon they be nearly sure to have go there to fee .
If you see a tailless jackal you will know that he be the one you want . '
So the panther thank him and go his way .
Now the jackal have guess what advice the old man would give his enemy , and so , while his friend be greedily eat the ripe melon in the sunny corner of the garden , he steal behind them and tie their tail together .
He have only just finish when his ear catch the sound of break branch ; and he cry : ` Quick !
quick !
here come the master of the garden ! '
And the jackal spring up and run away in all direction , leave their tail behind them .
And how be the panther to know which be his enemy ?
` They none of them have any tail , ' he say sadly to the old man , ` and I be tire of hunt them .
I shall leave them alone and go and catch something for supper . '
Of course the hedgehog have not be able to take part in any of these adventure ; but as soon a all danger be over , the jackal go to look for his friend , whom he be lucky enough to find at home .
` Ah , there you be , ' he say gaily . '
I have lose my tail since I saw you last .
And other people have lose theirs too ; but that be no matter !
I be hungry , so come with me to the shepherd who be sit over there , and we will ask him to sell u one of his sheep . '
` Yes , that be a good plan , ' answer the hedgehog .
And he walk as fast a his little leg would go to keep up with the jackal .
When they reach the shepherd the jackal pull out his purse from under his foreleg , and make his bargain .
` Only wait till to-morrow , ' say the shepherd , ` and I will give you the big sheep you ever saw .
But he always feed at some distance from the rest of the flock , and it would take me a long time to catch him . '
` Well , it be very tiresome , but I suppose I must wait , ' reply the jackal .
And he and the hedgehog look about for a nice dry cave in which to make themselves comfortable for the night .
But , after they have go , the shepherd kill one of his sheep , and strip off his skin , which he sew tightly round a greyhound he have with him , and put a cord round it neck .
Then he lay down and go to sleep .
Very , very early , before the sun be properly up , the jackal and the hedgehog be pull at the shepherd 's cloak .
` Wake up , ' they say , ` and give u that sheep .
We have have nothing to eat all night , and be very hungry . '
The shepherd yawn and rub his eye .
` He be tie up to that tree ; go and take him . '
So they go to the tree and unfasten the cord , and turn to go back to the cave where they have sleep , drag the greyhound after them .
When they reach the cave the jackal say to the hedgehog .
` Before I kill him let me see whether he be fat or thin . '
And he stand a little way back , so that he might the good examine the animal .
After look at him , with his head on one side , for a minute or two , he nod gravely .
` He be quite fat enough ; he be a good sheep . '
But the hedgehog , who sometimes show more cunning than anyone would have guess , answer : ` My friend , you be talk nonsense .
The wool be indeed a sheep 's wool , but the paw of my uncle the greyhound peep out from underneath . '
` He be a sheep , ' repeat the jackal , who do not like to think anyone clever than himself .
` Hold the cord while I look at him , ' answer the hedgehog .
Very unwillingly the jackal hold the rope , while the hedgehog walk slowly round the greyhound till he reach the jackal again .
He know quite well by the paw and tail that it be a greyhound and not a sheep , that the shepherd have sell them ; and a he could not tell what turn affair might take , he resolve to get out of the way .
` Oh !
yes , you be right , ' he say to the jackal ; ` but I never can eat till I have first drunk .
I will just go and quench my thirst from that spring at the edge of the wood , and then I shall be ready for breakfast . '
` Do n't be long , then , ' call the jackal , a the hedgehog hurry off at his best pace .
And he lay down under a rock to wait for him .
More than an hour pass by and the hedgehog have have plenty of time to go to the spring and back , and still there be no sign of him .
And this be very natural , a he have hide himself in some long grass under a tree !
At length the jackal guess that for some reason his friend have run away , and determine to wait for his breakfast no longer .
So he go up to the place where the greyhound have be tether and untie the rope .
But just a he be about to spring on his back and give him a deadly bite , the jackal hear a low growl , which never proceed from the throat of any sheep .
Like a flash of lightning the jackal throw down the cord and be fly across the plain ; but though his leg be long , the greyhound 's leg be long still , and he soon come up with his prey .
The jackal turn to fight , but he be no match for the greyhound , and in a few minute he be lie dead on the ground , while the greyhound be trot peacefully back to the shepherd .
The Adventures of the Jackal 's Eldest Son -LSB- Nouveaux Contes Berberes , par Rene Basset . -RSB-
Now , though the jackal be dead , he have leave two son behind him , every whit a cunning and tricky a their father .
The elder of the two be a fine handsome creature , who have a pleasant manner and make many friend .
The animal he saw most of be a hyena ; and one day , when they be take a walk together , they pick up a beautiful green cloak , which have evidently be drop by some one riding across the plain on a camel .
Of course each want to have it , and they almost quarrel over the matter ; but at length it be settle that the hyena should wear the cloak by day and the jackal by night .
After a little while , however , the jackal become discontent with this arrangement , declare that none of his friend , who be quite different from those of the hyena , could see the splendour of the mantle , and that it be only fair that he should sometimes be allow to wear it by day .
To this the hyena would by no mean consent , and they be on the eve of a quarrel when the hyena propose that they should ask the lion to judge between them .
The jackal agree to this , and the hyena wrap the cloak about him , and they both trot off to the lion 's den .
The jackal , who be fond of talk , at once tell the story ; and when it be finish the lion turn to the hyena and ask if it be true .
` Quite true , your majesty , ' answer the hyena .
` Then lay the cloak on the ground at my foot , ' say the lion , ` and I will give my judgment . '
So the mantle be spread upon the red earth , the hyena and the jackal stand on each side of it .
There be silence for a few moment , and then the lion sit up , look very great and wise .
` My judgment be that the garment shall belong wholly to whoever first ring the bell of the near mosque at dawn to-morrow .
Now go ; for much business awaits me ! '

You seem very serious about something . '

` What be the matter with you ? '
` Well , so many of the guest have bring their dog and mule with them , that I fear it may hardly be safe for you to go amongst them .
No ; do n't run off that way , ' he add quickly , ` because there be another troop that be come over the hill .
Lie down here , and I will throw these sack over you ; and keep still for your life , whatever happen . '
And what do happen be , that when the jackal be lie cover up , under a little hill , the hedgehog set a great stone rolling , which crush him to death .
The Adventures of the Younger Son of the Jackal -LSB- Contes Berberes . -RSB-
Now that the father and elder brother be both dead , all that be leave of the jackal family be one son , who be no less cunning than the others have be .
He do not like stay in the same place any good than they , and nobody ever know in what part of the country he might be find next .
One day , when we be wander about he behold a nice fat sheep , which be crop the grass and seem quite contented with her lot .
` Good morning , ' say the jackal , ' I be so glad to see you .
I have be look for you everywhere . '
` For ME ? '
answer the sheep , in an astonished voice ; ` but we have never meet before ! '
` No ; but I have hear of you .
Oh !
You do n't know what fine thing I have hear !
Ah , well , some people have all the luck ! '
` You be very kind , I be sure , ' answer the sheep , not know which way to look .
` Is there any way in which I can help you ? '
` There be something that I have set my heart on , though I hardly like to propose it on so short an acquaintance ; but from what people have tell me , I think that you and I might keep house together comfortably , if you would only agree to try .
I have several field belong to me , and if they be keep well watered they bear wonderful crop . '
` Perhaps I might come for a short time , ' say the sheep , with a little hesitation ; ` and if we do not get on , we can part company . '
` Oh , thank you , thank you , ' cry the jackal ; ` do not let u lose a moment . '
And he hold out his paw in such an inviting manner that the sheep get up and trot beside him till they reach home .
` Now , ' say the jackal , ` you go to the well and fetch the water , and I will pour it into the trench that run between the patch of corn . '
And a he do so he sing lustily .
The work be very hard , but the sheep do not grumble , and by-and-by be reward at see the little green head poke themselves through earth .
After that the hot sun ripen them quickly , and soon harvest time be come .
Then the grain be cut and ground and ready for sale .
When everything be complete , the jackal say to the sheep : ` Now let u divide it , so that we can each do what we like with his share . '
` You do it , ' answer the sheep ; ` here be the scale .
You must weigh it carefully . '
So the jackal begin to weigh it , and when he have finish , he count out loud : ` One , two , three , four , five , six , seven part for the jackal , and one part for the sheep .
If she like it she can take it , if not , she can leave it . '
The sheep look at the two heap in silence -- one so large , the other so small ; and then she answer : ` Wait for a minute , while I fetch some sack to carry away my share . '
But it be not sack that the sheep want ; for as soon a the jackal could no longer see her she set forth at her best pace to the home of the greyhound , where she arrive pant with the haste she have make .
` Oh , good uncle , help me , I pray you ! '
she cry , as soon a she could speak .
` Why , what be the matter ? '
ask the greyhound , look up with astonishment . '
I beg you to return with me , and frighten the jackal into pay me what he owe me , ' answer the sheep .
` For month we have live together , and I have twice every day draw the water , while he only pour it into the trench .
Together we have reap our harvest ; and now , when the moment to divide our crop have come , he have take seven part for himself , and only leave one for me . '
She finish , and give herself a twist , pass her woolly tail across her eye ; while the greyhound watch her , but hold his peace .
Then he say : ` Bring me a sack . '
And the sheep hasten away to fetch one .
Very soon she return , and lay the sack down before him .
` Open it wide , that I may get in , ' cry he ; and when he be comfortably roll up inside he bid the sheep take him on her back , and hasten to the place where she have leave the jackal .
She find him wait for her , and pretend to be asleep , though she clearly saw him wink one of his eye .
However , she take no notice , but throw the sack roughly on the ground , she exclaim : ` Now measure ! '
At this the jackal get up , and go to the heap of grain which lay close by , he divide it a before into eight portion -- seven for himself and one for the sheep .
` What be you do that for ? '
ask she indignantly .
` You know quite well that it be I who draw the water , and you who only pour it into the trench . '
` You be mistake , ' answer the jackal .
` It be I who draw the water , and you who pour it into the trench .
Anybody will tell you that !
If you like , I will ask those people who be dig there ! '
` Very well , ' reply the sheep .
And the jackal call out : ` Ho !
You digger , tell me : Who be it you hear sing over the work ? '
` Why , it be you , of course , jackal !
You sing so loud that the whole world might have hear you ! '
` And who it be that sings -- he who draw the water , or he who empty it ? '
` Why , certainly he who draw the water ! '
` You hear ? '
say the jackal , turn to the sheep .
` Now come and carry away your own portion , or else I shall take it for myself . '
` You have get the good of me , ' answer the sheep ; ` and I suppose I must confess myself beaten !
But a I bear no malice , go and eat some of the date that I have bring in that sack . '
And the jackal , who love date , run instantly back , and tore open the mouth of the sack .
But just a he be about to plunge his nose in he saw two brown eye calmly look at him .
In an instant he have let fall the flap of the sack and bound back to where the sheep be stand . '
I be only in fun ; and you have bring my uncle the greyhound .
Take away the sack , we will make the division over again . '
And he begin rearrange the heap .
` One , two , three , four , five , six , seven , for my mother the sheep , and one for the jackal , ' count he ; cast timid glance all the while at the sack .
` Now you can take your share and go , ' say the sheep .
And the jackal do not need twice tell !
Whenever the sheep look up , she still saw him fly , fly across the plain ; and , for all I know , he may be fly across it still .
The Three Treasures of the Giants -LSB- Contes Berberes , par Rene Basset . -RSB-
Long , long ago , there live an old man and his wife who have three son ; the eldest be call Martin , the second Michael , while the third be name Jack .
One evening they be all seat round the table , eat their supper of bread and milk .
` Martin , ' say the old man suddenly , ' I feel that I can not live much longer .
You , a the eldest , will inherit this hut ; but , if you value my blessing , be good to your mother and brother . '
` Certainly , father ; how can you suppose I should do them wrong ? '
reply Martin indignantly , help himself to all the best bit in the dish a he speak .
The old man saw nothing , but Michael look on in surprise , and Jack be so astonished that he quite forget to eat his own supper .
A little while after , the father fell ill , and send for his son , who be out hunting , to bid him farewell .
After give good advice to the two eldest , he turn to Jack .
` My boy , ' he say , ` you have not get quite as much sense a other people , but if Heaven have deprive you of some of your wit , it be give you a kind heart .
Always listen to what it say , and take heed to the word of your mother and brother , as well a you be able ! '
So say the old man sink back on his pillow and die .
The cry of grief utter by Martin and Michael sound through the house , but Jack remain by the bedside of his father , still and silent , a if he be dead also .
At length he get up , and go into the garden , hid himself in some tree , and wept like a child , while his two brother make ready for the funeral .
No sooner be the old man bury than Martin and Michael agree that they would go into the world together to seek their fortune , while Jack stay at home with their mother .
Jack would have like nothing well than to sit and dream by the fire , but the mother , who be very old herself , declare that there be no work for him to do , and that he must seek it with his brother .
So , one fine morning , all three set out ; Martin and Michael carry two great bag full of food , but Jack carry nothing .
This make his brother very angry , for the day be hot and the bag be heavy , and about noon they sit down under a tree and begin to eat .
Jack be as hungry a they be , but he know that it be no use ask for anything ; and he throw himself under another tree , and weep bitterly .
` Another time perhaps you wo n't be so lazy , and will bring food for yourself , ' say Martin , but to his surprise Jack answer : ` You be a nice pair !
You talk of seek your fortune so a not to be a burden on our mother , and you begin by carry off all the food she have in the house ! '
This reply be so unexpected that for some moment neither of the brother make any answer .
Then they offer their brother some of their food , and when he have finish eat they go their way once more .
Towards even they reach a small hut , and knock at the door , ask if they might spend the night there .
The man , who be a wood-cutter , invite them him , and beg them to sit down to supper .
Martin thank him , but be very proud , explain that it be only shelter they want , a they have plenty of food with them ; and he and Michael at once open their bag and begin to eat , while Jack hid himself in a corner .
The wife , on see this , take pity on him , and call him to come and share their supper , which he gladly do , and very good he find it .
At this , Martin regret deeply that he have be so foolish a to refuse , for his bit of bread and cheese seem very hard when he smelt the savoury soup his brother be enjoy .
` He sha n't have such a chance again , ' think he ; and the next morning he insist on plunge into a thick forest where they be likely to meet nobody .
For a long time they wander hither and thither , for they have no path to guide them ; but at last they come upon a wide clearing , in the midst of which stand a castle .
Jack shout with delight , but Martin , who be in a bad temper , say sharply : ` We must have take a wrong turning !
Let u go back . '
` Idiot ! '
replied Michael , who be hungry too , and , like many people when they be hungry , very cross also .
` We set out to travel through the world , and what do it matter if we go to the right or to the leave ? '
And , without another word , take the path to the castle , closely follow by Jack , and after a moment by Martin likewise .
The door of the castle stand open , and they enter a great hall , and look about them .
Not a creature be to be see , and suddenly Martin -- he do not know why -- felt a little frightened .
He would have leave the castle at once , but stop when Jack boldly walk up to a door in the wall and open it .
He could not for very shame be outdo by his young brother , and pass behind him into another splendid hall , which be fill from floor to ceiling with great piece of copper money .
The sight quite dazzle Martin and Michael , who empty all the provision that remain out of their bag , and heap them up instead with handful of copper .
Scarcely have they do this when Jack throw open another door , and this time it lead to a hall fill with silver .
In an instant his brother have turn their bag upside down , so that the copper money tumble out on to the floor , and be shovel in handful of the silver instead .
They have hardly finish , when Jack open yet a third door , and all three fell back in amazement , for this room a a mass of gold , so bright that their eye grow sore a they look at it .
However , they soon recover from their surprise , and quickly empty their bag of silver , and fill them with gold instead .
When they would hold no more , Martin say : ` We have well hurry off now l somebody else should come , and we might not know what to do ' ; and , follow by Michael , he hastily leave the castle .
Jack linger behind for a few minute to put piece of gold , silver , and copper into his pocket , and to eat the food that his brother have throw down in the first room .
Then he go after them , and find them lie down to rest in the midst of a forest .
It be near sunset , and Martin begin to feel hungry , so , when Jack arrive , he bid him return to the castle and bring the bread and cheese that they have leave there .
` It be hardly worth do that , ' answered Jack ; ` for I pick up the piece and eat them myself . '
At this reply both brother be beside themselves with anger , and fell upon the boy , beat him , and call him names , till they be quite tire .
` Go where you like , ' cry Martin with a final kick ; ` but never come near u again . '
And poor Jack ran weep into the wood .
The next morning his brother go home , and buy a beautiful house , where they live with their mother like great lord .
Jack remain for some hour in hiding , thankful to be safe from his tormentor ; but when no one come to trouble him , and his back do not ache so much , he begin to think what he have well do .
At length he make up his mind to go to the caste and take away as much money with him as would enable him to live in comfort for the rest of his life .
This be decide , he spring up , and set out along the path which lead to the castle .
As before , the door stand open , and he go on till he have reach the hall of gold , and there he take off his jacket and tie the sleeve together so that it might make a kind of bag .
He then begin to pour in the gold by handful , when , all at once , a noise like thunder shake the castle .
This be follow by a voice , hoarse a that of a bull , which cry : ' I smell the smell of a man . '
And two giant enter .
` So , little worm !
it be you who steal our treasure ! '
exclaim the big .
` Well , we have get you now , and we will cook you for supper ! '
But here the other giant draw him aside , and for a moment or two they whisper together .
At length the first giant spoke : ` To please my friend I will spare your life on condition that , for the future , you shall guard our treasure .
If you be hungry take this little table and rap on it , say , a you do so : `` The dinner of an emperor ! ''
and you will get as much food a you want . '
With a light heart Jack promise all that be ask of him , and for some day enjoy himself mightily .
He have everything he could wish for , and do nothing from morning till night ; but by-and-by he begin to get very tired of it all .
` Let the giant guard their treasure themselves , ' he say to himself at last ; ' I be go away .
But I will leave all the gold and silver behind me , and will take nought but you , my good little table . '
So , tuck the table under his arm , he start off for the forest , but he do not linger there long , and soon find himself in the field on the other side .
There he saw an old man , who beg Jack to give him something to eat .
` You could not have ask a good person , ' answer Jack cheerfully .
And sign to him to sit down with him under a tree , he set the table in front of them , and strike it three time , cry : ` The dinner of an emperor ! '
He have hardly utter the word when fish and meat of all kind appear on it !
` That be a clever trick of yours , ' say the old man , when he have eat as much a he want .
` Give it to me in exchange for a treasure I have which be still well .
Do you see this cornet ?
Well , you have only to tell it that you wish for an army , and you will have as many soldier a you require . '
Now , since he have be leave to himself , Jack have grow ambitious , so , after a moment 's hesitation , he take the cornet and give the table in exchange .
The old man bid him farewell , and set off down one path , while Jack choose another , and for a long time he be quite pleased with his new possession .
Then , a he felt hungry , he wish for his table back again , a no house be in sight , and he want some supper badly .
All at once he remember his cornet , and a wicked thought enter his mind .
` Two hundred hussar , forward ! '
cry he .
And the neighing of horse and the clanking of sword be hear close at hand .
The officer who ride at their head approach Jack , and politely inquire what he wish them to do . '
A mile or two along that road , ' answer Jack , ` you will find an old man carry a table .
Take the table from him and bring it to me . '
The officer salute and go back to his men , who start at a gallop to do Jack 's bidding .
In ten minute they have return , bear the table with them .
` That be all , thank you , ' say Jack ; and the soldier disappear inside the cornet .
Oh , what a good supper Jack have that night , quite forget that he owe it to a mean trick .
The next day he breakfast early , and then walk on towards the near town .
On the way thither he meet another old man , who beg for something to eat .
` Certainly , you shall have something to eat , ' reply Jack .
And , place the table on the ground he cry : ` The dinner of an emperor ! '
when all sort of food dish appear .
At first the old man ate quite greedily , and say nothing ; but , after his hunger be satisfied , he turn to Jack and say : ` That be a very clever trick of yours .
Give the table to me and you shall have something still well . ' '
I do n't believe that there be anything well , ' answer Jack .
` Yes , there be .
Here be my bag ; it will give you a many castle a you can possibly want . '
Jack thought for a moment ; then he reply : ` Very well , I will exchange with you . '
And pass the table to the old man , he hang the bag over his arm .
Five minute later he summon five hundred lancer out of the cornet and bid them go after the old man and fetch back the table .
Now that by his cunning he have obtain possession of the three magic object , he resolve to return to his native place .
Smearing his face with dirt , and tear his clothes so a to look like a beggar , he stop the passer by and , on pretence of seek money or food , he question them about the village gossip .
In this manner he learn that his brother have become great men , much respect in all the country round .
When he hear that , he lose no time in go to the door of their fine house and implore them to give him food and shelter ; but the only thing he get be hard word , and a command to beg elsewhere .
At length , however , at their mother 's entreaty , he be tell that he might pass the night in the stable .
Here he wait until everybody in the house be sound asleep , when he draw his bag from under his cloak , and desire that a castle might appear in that place ; and the cornet give him soldier to guard the castle , while the table furnish him with a good supper .
In the morning , he cause it all to vanish , and when his brother enter the stable they find him lie on the straw .
Jack remain here for many day , do nothing , and -- as far a anybody know -- eat nothing .
This conduct puzzle his brother greatly , and they put such constant question to him , that at length he tell them the secret of the table , and even give a dinner to them , which far outdo any they have ever see or hear of .
But though they have solemnly promise to reveal nothing , somehow or other the tale leak out , and before long reach the ear of the king himself .
That very even his chamberlain arrive at Jack 's dwelling , with a request from the king that he might borrow the table for three day .
` Very well , ' answer Jack , ` you can take it back with you .
But tell his majesty that if he do not return it at the end of the three day I will make war upon him . '
So the chamberlain carry away the table and take it straight to the king , tell him at the same time of Jack 's threat , at which they both laugh till their side ache .
Now the king be so delighted with the table , and the dinner it give him , that when the three day be over he could not make up his mind to part with it .
Instead , he send for his carpenter , and bid him copy it exactly , and when it be do he tell his chamberlain to return it to Jack with his best thanks .
It happen to be dinner time , and Jack invite the chamberlain , who know nothing of the trick , to stay and dine with him .
The good man , who have eat several excellent meal provide by the table in the last three day , accept the invitation with pleasure , even though he be to dine in a stable , and sit down on the straw beside Jack .
` The dinner of an emperor ! '
cry Jack .
But not even a morsel of cheese make it appearance .
` The dinner of an emperor ! '
shout Jack in a voice of thunder .
Then the truth dawn on him ; and , crush the table between his hand , he turn to the chamberlain , who , bewilder and half-frightened , be wonder how to get away .
` Tell your false king that to-morrow I will destroy his castle as easily a I have break this table . '
The chamberlain hasten back to the palace , and give the king Jack 's message , at which he laugh more than before , and call all his courtier to hear the story .
But they be not quite so merry when they wake next morning and beheld ten thousand horseman , and a many archer , surround the palace .
The king saw it be useless to hold out , and he take the white flag of truce in one hand , and the real table in the other , and set out to look for Jack . '
I commit a crime , ' say he ; ` but I will do my best to make up for it .
Here be your table , which I own with shame that I try to steal , and you shall have besides , my daughter a your wife ! '
There be no need to delay the marriage when the table be able to furnish the most splendid banquet that ever be see , and after everyone have eat and drink as much a they want , Jack take his bag and command a castle fill with all sort of treasure to arise in the park for himself and his bride .
At this proof of his power the king 's heart die within him .
` Your magic be great than mine , ' he say ; ` and you be young and strong , while I be old and tired .
Take , therefore , the sceptre from my hand , and my crown from my head , and rule my people good than I have do . '
So at last Jack 's ambition be satisfy .
He could not hope to be more than king , and as long a he have his cornet to provide him with soldier he be secure against his enemy .
He never forgive his brother for the way they have treat him , though he present his mother with a beautiful castle , and everything she could possibly wish for .
In the centre of his own palace be a treasure chamber , and in this chamber the table , the cornet , and the bag be keep a the most prized of all his possession , and not a week pass without a visit from king John to make sure they be safe .
He reign long and well , and die a very old man , beloved by his people .
But his good example be not follow by his son and his grandson .
They grow so proud that they be ashamed to think that the founder of their race have once be a poor boy ; and a they and all the world could not fail to remember it , as long a the table , the cornet , and the bag be show in the treasure chamber , one king , more foolish than the rest , thrust them into a dark and damp cellar .
For some time the kingdom remain , though it become weak and weak every year that pass .
Then , one day , a rumour reach the king that a large army be march against him .
Vaguely he recollect some tale he have hear about a magic cornet which could provide a many soldier a would serve to conquer the earth , and which have be remove by his grandfather to a cellar .
Thither he hasten that he might renew his power once more , and in that black and slimy spot he find the treasure indeed .
But the table fell to piece a he touch it , in the cornet there remain only a few fragment of leathern belt which the rat have gnaw , and in the bag nothing but broken bit of stone .
And the king bow his head to the doom that await him , and in his heart curse the ruin wrought by the pride and foolishness of himself and his forefather .
The Rover of the Plain -LSB- From Contes Populaires Slaves , par Louis Leger . -RSB-
A long way off , near the sea coast of the east of Africa , there dwelt , once upon a time , a man and his wife .
They have two child , a son and a daughter , whom they love very much , and , like parent in other country , they often talk of the fine marriages the young people would make some day .
Out there both boy and girl marry early , and very soon , it seem to the mother , a message be send by a rich man on the other side of the great hill offer a fat herd of ox in exchange for the girl .
Everyone in the house and in the village rejoice , and the maiden be despatch to her new home .
When all be quiet again the father say to his son : ` Now that we own such a splendid troop of ox you have well hasten and get yourself a wife , l some illness should overtake them .
Already we have see in the village round about one or two damsel whose parent would gladly part with them for less than half the herd .
Therefore tell u which you like best , and we will buy her for you . '
But the son answer : ` Not so ; the maiden I have see do not please me .
If , indeed , I must marry , let me travel and find a wife for myself . '
` It shall be a you wish , ' say the parent ; ` but if by-and-by trouble should come of it , it will be your fault and not ours . '
The youth , however , would not listen ; and bid his father and mother farewell , set out on his search .
Far , far away he wander , over mountain and across river , till he reach a village where the people be quite different from those of his own race .
He glance about him and notice that the girl be fair to look upon , a they pound maize or stew something that smelt very nice in earthen pot -- especially if you be hot and tire ; and when one of the maiden turn round and offer the stranger some dinner , he make up his mind that he would wed her and nobody else .
So he send a message to her parent ask their leave to take her for his wife , and they come next day to bring their answer .
` We will give you our daughter , ' say they , ` if you can pay a good price for her .
Never be there so hardworking a girl ; and how we shall do without her we can not tell !
Still -- no doubt your father and mother will come themselves and bring the price ? '
` No ; I have the price with me , ' reply the young man ; lay down a handful of gold piece .
` Here it be -- take it . '
The old couple 's eye glitter greedily ; but custom forbid them to touch the price before all be arrange .
` At least , ' say they , after a moment 's pause , ` we may expect them to fetch your wife to her new home ? '
` No ; they be not use to travel , ' answer the bridegroom .
` Let the ceremony be perform without delay , and we will set forth at once .
It be a long journey . '
Then the parent call in the girl , who be lie in the sun outside the hut , and , in the presence of all the village , a goat be kill , the sacred dance take place , and a blessing be say over the head of the young people .
After that the bride be lead aside by her father , whose duty it be to bestow on her some part advice a to her conduct in her married life .
` Be good to your husband 's parent , ' add he , ` and always do the will of your husband . '
And the girl nod her head obediently .
Next it be the mother 's turn ; and , a be the custom of the tribe , she speak to her daughter : ` Will you choose which of your sister shall go with you to cut your wood and carry your water ? ' '
I do not want any of them , ' answer she ; ` they be no use .
They will drop the wood and spill the water . '
` Then will you have any of the other child ?
There be enough to spare , ' ask the mother again .
But the bride say quickly : ' I will have none of them !
You must give me our buffalo , the Rover of the Plain ; he alone shall serve me . '
` What folly you talk ! '
cry the parent .
` Give you our buffalo , the Rover of the Plain ?
Why , you know that our life depend on him .
Here he be well feed and lie on soft grass ; but how can you tell what will befall him in another country ?
The food may be bad , he will die of hunger ; and , if he die we die also . '
` No , no , ' say the bride ; ' I can look after him as well a you .
Get him ready , for the sun be sink and it be time we set forth . '
So she go away and put together a small pot fill with healing herm , a horn that she use in tend sick people , a little knife , and a calabash contain deer fat ; and , hide these about her , she take leave of her father and mother and start across the mountain by the side of her husband .
But the young man do not see the buffalo that follow them , which have leave his home to be the servant of his wife .
No one ever know how the news spread to the kraal that the young man be come back , bring a wife with him ; but , somehow or other , when the two enter the village , every man and woman be stand in the road utter shout of welcome .
` Ah , you be not dead after all , ' cry they ; ` and have find a wife to your liking , though you would have none of our girl .
Well , well , you have choose your own path ; and if ill come of it beware lest you grumble . '
Next day the husband take his wife to the field and show her which be his , and which belong to his mother .
The girl listen carefully to all he tell her , and walk with him back to the hut ; but close to the door she stop , and say : ' I have drop my necklace of bead in the field , and I must go and look for it . '
But in truth she have do nothing of the sort , and it be only an excuse to go and seek the buffalo .
The beast be crouch under a tree when she come up , and snort with pleasure at the sight of her .
` You can roam about this field , and this , and this , ' she say , ` for they belong to my husband ; and that be his wood , where you may hide yourself .
But the other field be his mother 's , so beware l you touch them . ' '
I will beware , ' answer the buffalo ; and , pat his head , the girl leave him .
Oh , how much well a servant he be than any of the little girl the bride have refuse to bring with her !
If she want water , she have only to cross the patch of maize behind the hut and seek out the place where the buffalo lay hide , and put down her pail beside him .
Then she would sit at her ease while he go to the lake and bring the bucket back brimming over .
If she want wood , he would break the branch off the tree and lay them at her foot .
And the villager watch her return laden , and say to each other : ` Surely the girl of her country be strong than our girl , for none of them could cut so quickly or carry so much ! '
But then , nobody know that she have a buffalo for a servant .
Only , all this time she never give the poor buffalo anything to eat , because she have just one dish , out of which she and her husband ate ; while in her old home there be a dish put aside expressly for the Rover of the Plain .
The buffalo bore it as long a he could ; but , one day , when his mistress bid him go to the lake and fetch water , his knee almost give way from hunger .
He keep silence , however , till the evening , when he say to his mistress : ' I be nearly starve ; I have not touch food since I come here .
I can work no more . '
` Alas ! '
answer she , ` what can I do ?
I have only one dish in the house .
You will have to steal some bean from the field .
Take a few here and a few there ; but be sure not to take too many from one place , or the owner may notice it . '

And when at last his hunger be satisfied , he creep back to his lair .
But a buffalo be not a fairy , and the next morning , when the woman arrive to work in the field , they stand still with astonishment , and say to each other : ` Just look at this ; a savage beast have be destroy our crop , and we can see the trace of his foot ! '
