Once upon a time there live a king and queen who love each other dearly , and would have be perfectly happy if they have only have a little son or daughter to play with .
They never talk about it , and always pretend that there be nothing in the world to wish for ; but , sometimes when they look at other people 's child , their face grow sad , and their courtier and attendant know the reason why .
One day the queen be sit alone by the side of a waterfall which sprung from some rock in the large park adjoin the castle .
She be feel more than usually miserable , and have send away her lady so that no one might witness her grief .

she ask , turn to her guide ; who answer : ` Oh , that be the fairy ' palace , and here be some of them come to meet u . '

` My princess !
O my dear princess ! '
cry she ; and again the white doe rub her head against her , for think the spiteful fairy have take away her power of speech , she have not deprive her of her reason !
All day long the two remain together , and when Eglantine grow hungry she be lead by the white doe to a part of the forest where pear and peach grow in abundance ; but , a night come on , the maid of honour be fill with the terror of wild beast which have beset the princess during her first night in the forest .
` Is there no hut or cave we could go into ? '
ask she .
But the doe only shake her head ; and the two sit down and weep with fright .
The fairy Tulip , who , in spite of her anger , be very soft-hearted , be touch at their distress , and fly quickly to their help . '
I can not take away the spell altogether , ' she say , ` for the Fairy of the Fountain be strong than I ; but I can shorten the time of your punishment , and be able to make it less hard , for as soon a darkness fall you shall resume your own shape . '
To think that by-and-by she would cease to be a white doe -- indeed , that she would at once cease to be one during the night -- be for the present joy enough for Desiree , and she skip about on the grass in the prettiest manner .
` Go straight down the path in front of you , ' continue the fairy , smile a she watch her ; ` go straight down the path and you will soon reach a little hut where you will find shelter . '
And with these word she vanish , leave her hearer happy than they ever think they could be again .
An old woman be stand at the door of the hut when Eglantine draw near , with the white doe trotting by her side .
` Good evening ! '
she say ; ` could you give me a night 's lodging for myself and my doe ? '
` Certainly I can , ' reply the old woman .
And she lead them into a room with two little white bed , so clean and comfortable that it make you sleepy even to look at them .
The door have hardly close behind the old woman when the sun sink below the horizon , and Desiree become a girl again .
` Oh , Eglantine !
what should I have do if you have not follow me , ' she cry .
And she fling herself into her friend 's arm in a transport of delight .
Early in the morning Eglantine be awaken by the sound of someone scratching at the door , and on open her eye she saw the white doe struggle to get out .
The little creature look up and into her face , and nod her head a the maid of honour unfasten the latch , but bound away into the wood , and be lose to sight in a moment .
Meanwhile , the prince and Becasigue be wander through the wood , till at last the prince grow so tired , that he lay down under a tree , and tell Becasigue that he have well go in search of food , and of some place where they could sleep .
Becasigue have not go very far , when a turn of the path bring him face to face with the old woman who be feed her dove before her cottage .
` Could you give me some milk and fruit ? '
ask he . '
I be very hungry myself , and , besides , I have leave a friend behind me who be still weak from illness . '
` Certainly I can , ' answer the old woman .
` But come and sit down in my kitchen while I catch the goat and milk it . '
Becasigue be glad enough to do a he be bid , and in a few minute the old woman return with a basket brimming over with orange and grape .
` If your friend have be ill he should not pass the night in the forest , ' say she . '
I have room in my hut -- tiny enough , it be true ; but good than nothing , and to that you be both heartily welcome . '
Becasigue thank her warmly , and a by this time it be almost sunset , he set out to fetch the prince .
It be while he be absent that Eglantine and the white doe enter the hut , and have , of course , no idea that in the very next room be the man whose childish impatience have be the cause of all their trouble .
In spite of his fatigue , the prince sleep badly , and directly it be light he rise , and bidding Becasigue remain where he be , a he wish to be alone , he stroll out into the forest .
He walk on slowly , just a his fancy lead him , till , suddenly , he come to a wide open space , and in the middle be the white doe quietly eat her breakfast .
She bound off at the sight of a man , but not before the prince , who have fasten on his bow without thinking , have let fly several arrow , which the fairy Tulip take care should do her no harm .
But , quickly a she run , she soon felt her strength fail her , for fifteen year of life in a tower have not teach her how to exercise her limb .
Luckily , the prince be too weak to follow her far , and a turn of a path bring her close to the hut , where Eglantine be await her .
Panting for breath , she enter their room , and fling herself down on the floor .
When it be dark again , and she be once more the princess Desiree , she tell Eglantine what have befall her . '
I fear the Fairy of the Fountain , and the cruel beast , ' say she ; ` but somehow I never think of the danger that I run from men .
I do not know now what save me . '
` You must stay quietly here till the time of your punishment be over , ' answered Eglantine .
But when the morning dawn , and the girl turn into a doe , the longing for the forest come over her , and she spring away a before .
As soon a the prince be awake he hasten to the place where , only the day before , he have find the white doe feeding ; but of course she have take care to go in the opposite direction .
Much disappointed , he try first one green path and then another , and at last , weary with walking , he throw himself down and go fast asleep .
Just at this moment the white doe spring out of a thicket near by , and start back trembling when she behold her enemy lie there .
Yet , instead of turn to fly , something bid her go and look at him unseen .
As she gaze a thrill run through her , for she felt that , worn and waste though he be by illness , it be the face of her destined husband .
Gently stoop over him she kiss his forehead , and at her touch he awake .
For a minute they look at each other , and to his amazement he recognize the white doe which have escape him the previous day .
But in an instant the animal be arouse to a sense of her danger , and she flee with all her strength into the thick part of the forest .
Quick a lightning the prince be on her track , but this time it be with no wish to kill or even wound the beautiful creature .
` Pretty doe !
pretty doe !
stop !
I wo n't hurt you , ' cry he , but his word be carry away by the wind .
At length the doe could run no more , and when the prince reach her , she be lie stretch out on the grass , wait for her death blow .
But instead the prince knelt at her side , and stroke her , and bid her fear nothing , a he would take care of her .
So he fetch a little water from the stream in his horn hunt cup , then , cut some branch from the tree , he twist them into a litter which he cover with moss , and lay the white doe gently on it .
For a long time they remain thus , but when Desiree saw by the way that the light strike the tree , that he sun must be near it setting , she be fill with alarm lest the darkness should fall , and the prince should behold her in her human shape .
` No , he must not see me for the first time here , ' she think , and instantly begin to plan how to get rid of him .
Then she open her mouth and let her tongue hang out , a if she be die of thirst , and the prince , a she expect , hasten to the stream to get her some more water .
When he return , the white doe be go .
That night Desiree confess to Eglantine that her pursuer be no other than the prince , and that far from flatter him , the portrait have never do him justice .
` Is it not hard to meet him in this shape , ' wept she , ` when we both love each other so much ? '
But Eglantine comfort her , and remind her that in a short time all would be well .
The prince be very angry at the flight of the white doe , for whom he have take so much trouble , and return to the cottage he pour out his adventure and his wrath to Becasigue , who could not help smile .
` She shall not escape me again , ' cry the prince .
` If I hunt her every day for a year , I will have her at last . '
And in this frame of mind he go to bed .
When the white doe enter the forest next morning , she have not make up her mind whether she would go and meet the prince , or whether she would shun him , and hide in thicket of which he know nothing .
She decide that the last plan be the best ; and so it would have be if the prince have not take the very same direction in search of her .
Quite by accident he catch sight of her white skin shin through the bush , and at the same instant she hear a twig snap under his foot .
In a moment she be up and away , but the prince , not know how else to capture her , aim an arrow at her leg , which bring her to the ground .
The young man felt like a murderer a he run hastily up to where the white doe lay , and do his best to soothe the pain she felt , which , in reality , be the last part of the punishment send by the Fairy of the Fountain .
First he bring her some water , and then he fetch some healing herb , and have crush them in his hand , lay them on the wound .
` Ah !
what a wretch I be to have hurt you , ' cry he , rest her head upon his knee ; ` and now you will hate me and fly from me for ever ! '
For some time the doe lay quietly where she be , but , a before , she remember that the hour of her transformation be near .
She struggle to her foot , but the prince would not hear of her walking , and think the old woman might be able to dress her wound well than he could , he take her in his arm to carry her back to the hut .
But , small a she be , she make herself so heavy that , after stagger a few step under her weight , he lay her down , and tie her fast to a tree with some of the ribbon of his hat .
This do he go away to get help .
Meanwhile Eglantine have grow very uneasy at the long absence of her mistress , and have come out to look for her .
Just a the prince pass out of sight the fluttering ribbon dance before her eye , and she descry her beautiful princess bound to a tree .
With all her might she work at the knot , but not a single one could she undo , though all appear so easy .
She be still busy with them when a voice behind her say : ` Pardon me , fair lady , but it be MY doe you be try to steal ! '
` Excuse me , good knight ' answered Eglantine , hardly glance at him , ` but it be MY doe that be tie up here !
And if you wish for a proof of it , you can see if she know me or not .
Touch my heart , my little one , ' she continue , drop on her knee .
And the doe lift up it fore-foot and lay it on her side .
` Now put your arm round my neck , and sigh . '
And again the doe do a she be bid .
` You be right , ' say the prince ; ` but it be with sorrow I give her up to you , for though I have wound her yet I love her deeply . '
To this Eglantine answer nothing ; but carefully raise up the doe , she lead her slowly to the hut .
Now both the prince and Becasigue be quite unaware that the old woman have any guest besides themselves , and , follow afar , be much surprise to behold Eglantine and her charge enter the cottage .
They lose no time in question the old woman , who reply that she know nothing about the lady and her white doe , who sleep next the chamber occupy by the prince and his friend , but that they be very quiet , and pay her well .
Then she go back to her kitchen .
` Do you know , ' say Becasigue , when they be alone , ' I be certain that the lady we saw be the maid of honour to the Princess Desiree , whom I meet at the palace .
And , a her room be next to this , it will be easy to make a small hole through which I can satisfy myself whether I be right or not . '
So , take a knife out of his pocket , he begin to saw away the woodwork .
The girl hear the grating noise , but fancy it be a mouse , pay no attention , and Becasigue be leave in peace to pursue his work .
At length the hole be large enough for him to peep through , and the sight be one to strike him dumb with amazement .
He have guess truly : the tall lady be Eglantine herself ; but the other -- where have he see her ?
Ah !
now he know -- it be the lady of the portrait !
Desiree , in a flowing dress of green silk , be lie stretch out upon cushion , and a Eglantine bent over her to bathe the wounded leg , she begin to talk : ` Oh !
let me die , ' cry she , ` rather than go on lead this life .
You can not tell the misery of be a beast all the day , and unable to speak to the man I love , to whose impatience I owe my cruel fate .
Yet , even so , I can not bring myself to hate him . '
These word , low though they be speak , reach Becasigue , who could hardly believe his ear .
He stand silent for a moment ; then , cross to the window out of which the prince be gaze , he take his arm and lead him across the room .
